# Sound API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The Sound API lets Lua scripts load and play audio files with real-time volume and stereo panning control.

Sound files are loaded from relative paths resolved against your script directory (same as the File System API).

**Supported formats:** WAV (PCM 8/16-bit), MP3, AAC, WMA, FLAC — anything Windows Media Foundation can decode.

All audio is resampled to 44100 Hz stereo at load time. Up to 64 sounds can play simultaneously.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#concepts)

Concepts

There are two handle types, both represented as integers:

*   **Sound handle** — a loaded audio resource returned by `load_sound`. Can be played multiple times simultaneously. Must be freed with `free_sound` when no longer needed.
    
*   **Instance handle** — a single playing occurrence returned by `play_sound`. Used to stop, query, or adjust an active playback.
    

Both return `0` on failure. All functions are safe to call with `0` handles (they become no-ops).

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#loading-and-freeing)

Loading & Freeing

`**load_sound(path) -> handle**`

Loads a sound file from a relative path.

*   `path` (string) — Relative path to the audio file (e.g. `"sounds/hit.wav"`, `"alert.mp3"`).
    

Returns a sound handle (integer), or `0` if the file doesn't exist or decoding fails.

* * *

`**free_sound(handle)**`

Frees a previously loaded sound resource. Any active instances using this sound are stopped automatically.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#playback)

Playback

`**play_sound(sound [, volume [, pan [, loop]]]) -> instance**`

Plays a loaded sound and returns an instance handle.

*   `sound` (integer) — Sound handle from `load_sound`.
    
*   `volume` (number) — `0.0` (silent) to `1.0` (full). Default `1.0`. Clamped.
    
*   `pan` (number) — `-1.0` (full left) to `+1.0` (full right). Default `0.0` (center). Clamped.
    
*   `loop` (boolean) — If `true`, the sound repeats until explicitly stopped. Default `false`.
    

Returns an instance handle (integer), or `0` if the sound handle is invalid or all 64 instance slots are in use.

* * *

`**stop_sound(instance)**`

Stops a playing instance immediately.

* * *

`**stop_all_sounds()**`

Stops every currently playing sound instance.

* * *

`**is_sound_playing(instance) -> bool**`

Returns `true` if the instance is still actively playing. Returns `false` if it finished, was stopped, or the handle is invalid.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#live-adjustment)

Live Adjustment

These functions modify a playing instance in real time. Changes take effect on the next mixer tick (~20ms).

`**set_sound_volume(instance, volume)**`

Changes volume of a playing instance. `0.0` to `1.0`, clamped.

* * *

`**set_sound_pan(instance, pan)**`

Changes stereo panning of a playing instance. `-1.0` (left) to `+1.0` (right), clamped.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#examples)

Examples

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#play-a-one-shot-sound-effect)

Play a one-shot sound effect

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#looping-background-music)

Looping background music

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#directional-sound-with-panning)

Directional sound with panning

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#fade-out-over-time)

Fade out over time

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#multiple-simultaneous-sounds)

Multiple simultaneous sounds

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#notes)

Notes

*   Sound data is fully decoded to PCM at load time. Loading is the expensive operation — `play_sound` is cheap.
    
*   Instance handles point into a fixed pool of 64 slots. If all slots are in use, `play_sound` returns `0`.
    
*   Calling `free_sound` automatically stops all instances that reference that sound.
    
*   Sounds are automatically freed when your script is unloaded (leaked handles are cleaned up). You should still free sounds explicitly when possible.
    
*   The `path` parameter follows the same validation rules as the File System API: relative paths only, no `..` segments, no `:` characters.
    

[PreviousUtilitieschevron-left](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities)
[NextCS2 Extended APIchevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/cs2-extended-api)

Last updated 1 month ago

*   [Concepts](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#concepts)
    
*   [Loading & Freeing](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#loading-and-freeing)
    
*   [Playback](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#playback)
    
*   [Live Adjustment](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#live-adjustment)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#examples)
    
*   [Notes](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api#notes)
    

Copy

    local snd = 0
    
    function main()
        snd = load_sound("pop.mp3")
        if snd == 0 then
            log("Failed to load sound")
            return 0
        end
    
        play_sound(snd, 0.8, 0.0)
        return 1
    end
    
    function on_unload()
        if snd ~= 0 then free_sound(snd) end
    end

Copy

    local music = 0
    local music_inst = 0
    
    function main()
        music = load_sound("ambient.ogg")
        if music ~= 0 then
            music_inst = play_sound(music, 0.5, 0.0, true)
        end
        return 1
    end
    
    function on_unload()
        if music_inst ~= 0 then stop_sound(music_inst) end
        if music ~= 0 then free_sound(music) end
    end

Copy

    local function play_hit(snd, target_x, player_x, max_range)
        local pan = (target_x - player_x) / max_range
        if pan < -1.0 then pan = -1.0 end
        if pan >  1.0 then pan =  1.0 end
    
        play_sound(snd, 1.0, pan)
    end

Copy

    local snd = 0
    local inst = 0
    local vol = 1.0
    
    function main()
        snd = load_sound("alert.wav")
        if snd == 0 then return 0 end
    
        inst = play_sound(snd, 1.0, 0.0)
        return 1
    end
    
    function on_frame()
        if inst == 0 then return end
    
        vol = vol - 0.02
        if vol <= 0.0 then
            stop_sound(inst)
            inst = 0
            return
        end
    
        set_sound_volume(inst, vol)
    end
    
    function on_unload()
        if inst ~= 0 then stop_sound(inst) end
        if snd ~= 0 then free_sound(snd) end
    end

Copy

    function main()
        local snd = load_sound("hit.wav")
        if snd == 0 then return 0 end
    
        play_sound(snd, 1.0,  0.0)
        play_sound(snd, 0.7, -0.5)
        play_sound(snd, 0.5,  0.8)
    
        return 1
    end

---

# Json API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The JSON API provides simple, fast parsing and encoding of JSON using native Lua data types. All JSON features are exposed under the global `json` table.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#overview)

Overview

The `json` module supports:

Operation

Description

`**json.parse(str)**`

Parse a JSON string into Lua values

`**json.decode(str)**`

Alias of `json.parse`

`**json.stringify(value)**`

Convert Lua values into JSON

`**json.encode(value)**`

Alias of `json.stringify`

The API is intentionally minimal and strictly uses plain Lua tables, numbers, booleans, strings, and `nil`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#json-lua-json.parse-json.decode)

JSON → Lua: `json.parse` / `json.decode`

Copy

    value, err = json.parse(string)
    value, err = json.decode(string)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#parameters)

Parameters

*   **string** — a UTF-8 JSON text.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#returns)

Returns

*   On success: **Lua value representing the JSON structure**
    
*   On error: `nil, "error message"`
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#lua-type-mapping)

Lua Type Mapping

JSON

Lua

Object `{}`

Table `{ key = value }`

Array `[]`

Table `{ [1] = ..., [2] = ... }`

`"text"`

string

`123`

number

`true` / `false`

boolean

`null`

`**nil**` (field disappears when iterating!)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#example)

Example

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#invalid-json-example)

Invalid JSON example

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#lua-json-json.stringify-json.encode)

Lua → JSON: `json.stringify` / `json.encode`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#parameters-1)

Parameters

*   **value** — any Lua value (table / string / number / boolean / nil)
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#returns-1)

Returns

*   On success: **string containing JSON**
    
*   On failure: `nil, "error message"`
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#supported-lua-types)

Supported Lua Types

Lua

JSON

String

`"text"`

Number

`123` or `1.23`

Boolean

`true` / `false`

Table

Object or Array _(auto-detected)_

nil

`null` _(inside tables only)_

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#array-vs-object-detection)

Array vs Object Detection

Lua tables are encoded as JSON arrays **only** if they contain:

*   continuous integer keys
    
*   starting from `1`
    
*   with no gaps
    

Otherwise they become JSON objects.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#example-1)

Example

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#mixed-tables)

Mixed Tables

Tables with both numeric and string keys become JSON objects:

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#round-trip-example)

Round-Trip Example

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#null-handling)

Null Handling

JSON `null` becomes **Lua** `**nil**`.

This means fields may “disappear” from tables:

This is correct behavior and matches typical JSON–Lua conventions.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#error-handling)

Error Handling

All functions safely return:

Examples of failure:

*   malformed JSON
    
*   unsupported Lua type (function, userdata, thread)
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#summary)

Summary

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api#functions-provided)

Functions Provided

Function

Description

`json.parse(str)`

Parse JSON into Lua values

`json.decode(str)`

Alias of parse

`json.stringify(val)`

Encode Lua value into JSON

`json.encode(val)`

Alias of stringify

Copy

    local data, err = json.parse('{"a":1,"b":[10,20],"flag":true}')
    print(data.a)         --> 1
    print(data.b[1])      --> 10
    print(data.flag)      --> true

Copy

    local v, e = json.parse("{ broken json }")
    if not v then
        print("Parse failed:", e)
    end

Copy

    json_str, err = json.stringify(value)
    json_str, err = json.encode(value)

Copy

    local obj = {
        hello = "world",
        numbers = { 1, 2, 3 }
    }
    
    local json_str = json.stringify(obj)
    print(json_str)
    -- {"hello":"world","numbers":[1,2,3]}

Copy

    local t = { [1] = "first", [3] = "third", foo = "bar" }
    print(json.stringify(t))
    -- {"3":"third","1":"first","foo":"bar"}

Copy

    local original = {
        text = "hello",
        list = { 10, 20, 30 },
        nested = { a = 1, b = { "x", "y" } }
    }
    
    local encoded = json.stringify(original)
    local decoded = json.parse(encoded)
    
    -- decoded now matches `original`

Copy

    local obj = json.parse('{"a":1,"b":null,"c":2}')
    -- obj = { a = 1, c = 2 }

Copy

    nil, "error message"

# Input API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The Input API provides access to mouse, keyboard, and UI-hover information from Lua scripts. These functions are intended to be used inside `on_frame()`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#mouse-input)

🖱 Mouse Input

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#mouse-position)

Mouse Position

Copy

    x, y = get_mouse_pos()

Returns the cursor position **inside the game/overlay window**.

Copy

    x, y = get_mouse_pos_desktop()

Returns the cursor position in **desktop/screen coordinates**.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#mouse-delta)

Mouse Delta

Copy

    dx, dy = get_mouse_delta()

Movement since last frame in overlay space.

Copy

    dx, dy = get_mouse_delta_desktop()

Movement since last frame in desktop space.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#scroll-wheel)

Scroll Wheel

Copy

    amount = get_scroll_delta()

Positive for scroll up, negative for scroll down.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#movement-event)

Movement Event

Returns `true` if the mouse moved this frame.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#hover-detection)

Hover Detection

Returns `true` if the mouse is inside the rectangle `(x, y, w, h)`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#keyboard-input)

⌨️ Keyboard Input

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#key-down)

Key Down

Returns `true` while key is held.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#raw-down)

Raw Down

Reflects OS-level down state before filtering.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#fired)

Fired

Behaves like text input

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#toggle)

Toggle

Toggles each time the key is pressed (flip-flop behavior).

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#single-press)

Single Press

True only on the **first frame** the key is pressed.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#previous-state)

Previous State

State from the previous frame.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#full-key-state)

🔍 Full Key State

Returns all internal state fields for a virtual key.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#keys-down-list)

🧩 Keys Down List

Returns a Lua table of all currently pressed virtual keys.

Example:

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#text-input-and-key-names)

📝 Text Input & Key Names

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#recent-typed-characters)

Recent Typed Characters

Returns a string of recently typed characters (from your internal text buffer).

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#key-name)

Key Name

Returns a readable name like `"SPACE"`, `"A"`, `"SHIFT"`.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#example)

📌 Example


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api#notes)

💡 Notes


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `vk` refers to Windows Virtual-Key codes (e.g., `0x41` = `'A'`, `0x20` = Space).
    
*   The Input API is frame-based and intended to be called from inside `on_frame()`.
    
*   `get_recent_key_input()` is ideal for text input boxes or consoles.

[NextProc APIchevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api)

Copy

    moved = mouse_movement_received()

Copy

    hovered = is_hovered(x, y, w, h) --overlay window

Copy

    down = key_down(vk)

Copy

    raw = key_raw_down(vk)

Copy

    fired = key_fired(vk)

Copy

    toggle = key_toggle(vk)

Copy

Copy

Copy

    raw_down, down, fired, toggle, single, prev =
        get_key_state(vk)

Copy

    keys = get_keys_down()

Copy

    for i, vk in ipairs(get_keys_down()) do
        log("Down: " .. get_key_name(vk))
    end

Copy

    txt = get_recent_key_input()

Copy

    name = get_key_name(vk)

Copy

    local font = 0
    local frame = 0
    local last_keys = ""
    
    function main()
        log("Lua Input Test Script Loaded!")
        font = get_font20()
        return 1
    end
    
    function on_frame()
        frame = frame + 1
        
        local vw, vh = get_view()
        local scale = get_view_scale()
        
        local mx, my = get_mouse_pos()
        local dx, dy = get_mouse_delta()
        local scroll = get_scroll_delta()
        
        local keys = get_keys_down()
        local recent = get_recent_key_input()
        
        -- Panel
        local w = 450 * scale
        local h = 300 * scale
        local x = 20 * scale
        local y = 20 * scale
        
        draw_rect_filled(
            x, y, w, h,
            20, 20, 25, 220,
            8 * scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
            )
        
        draw_rect(
            x, y, w, h,
            60, 120, 255, 255,
            2 * scale,
            8 * scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
            )
        
        local function text(label, value, ox, oy)
            draw_text(
                label .. value,
                x + 10 * scale, y + oy * scale,
                255, 255, 255, 255,
                font,
                TE_SHADOW,
                0,0,0,180,
                1.0,
                true
                )
        end
        
        text("Mouse Pos: ", string.format("%0.1f, %0.1f", mx, my), 10, 10)
        text("Mouse Delta: ", string.format("%0.2f, %0.2f", dx, dy), 10, 40)
        text("Scroll: ", tostring(scroll), 10, 70)
        
        -- Hover test
        local hx, hy, hw, hh = vw*0.5 - 50*scale, vh*0.5 - 50*scale, 100*scale, 100*scale
        local hovered = is_hovered(hx, hy, hw, hh)
        
        draw_rect_filled(
            hx, hy, hw, hh,
            hovered and 60 or 30,
            hovered and 200 or 60,
            hovered and 80 or 60,
            240,
            8*scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
            )
        
        text("Hovered (center box): ", hovered and "true" or "false", 10, 100)
        
        -- Key states
        local space_down = key_down(0x20)
        local space_name = get_key_name(0x20) or "?"
        
        text("SPACE down: ", tostring(space_down), 10, 130)
        text("SPACE name: ", space_name, 10, 190)
        
        -- Keys currently down
        local kd = ""
        for i,vk in ipairs(keys) do
            kd = kd .. get_key_name(vk) .. " "
        end  
        text("Keys down: ", kd, 10, 220)
        
        -- Recent typed characters
        if recent ~= "" then
            last_keys = recent
        end
        text("Recent typed: ", last_keys, 10, 250)
    end
    
    function on_unload()
        log("Lua Input Test Script Unloaded")
    end

# Engine Specific API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal-engine-helpers-unreal_engine)

Unreal Engine Helpers (`unreal_engine`)

The `unreal_engine` table contains helpers for working with Unreal Engine games (UE4 / UE5).

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.read_tarray)

`unreal_engine.read_tarray`

Copy

    unreal_engine.read_tarray(proc, tarray_address[, max_count]) -> table

Reads an Unreal-style dynamic array (`TArray`) and returns its contents as a Lua array of pointers.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object used for reading game memory.
    
*   `tarray_address` Integer address of the array in game memory.
    
*   `max_count` _(optional, default: 4096)_ Maximum number of elements to read. Used as a safety limit.
    

**Returns**

*   A Lua array table indexed from `1` upward, containing integer addresses (pointers).
    
*   If anything is invalid (bad address, null pointer, weird count), an **empty table** is returned.
    

**Example**

Copy

    local actors = unreal_engine.read_tarray(proc, actors_array_addr, 1024)
    
    for i, actor_ptr in ipairs(actors) do
        -- actor_ptr is an integer address inside the game
    end

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info)

`unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info`

Reads a camera/view structure and converts it into a normalized Lua table.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `view_info_address` Address of the camera/view information in memory.
    

**Returns**

A table with this structure:

If the address or process is invalid, an **empty table** is returned.

**Example**

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64)

`unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64`

Same purpose as `read_minimal_view_info`, but for layouts that use **double-precision** values (common in some UE5 setups).

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `view_info_address` Address of the camera/view information in memory.
    

**Returns**

Same shape as the float version:

If inputs are invalid, returns an **empty table**.

**Example**

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal_engine.world_to_screen)

`unreal_engine.world_to_screen`

Projects a point from world space to screen space using camera data.

**Parameters**

*   `world_position` Can be either:
    
    *   A table: `{ x = number, y = number, z = number }`, or
        
    *   Three numbers: `x, y, z`
        
    
*   `view_info` The camera table returned from:
    
    *   `unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info`, or
        
    *   `unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64`
        
    
    Must contain:
    

**Returns**

*   On success (point is in front of the camera):
    
*   If the point is behind the camera: `nil`.
    
*   If input is invalid: a Lua error is raised.
    

**Example**

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#world-to-screen-projection)

World-to-Screen Projection

Convert 3D world coordinates to 2D screen positions using view matrices.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#fortnite-helper)

Fortnite Helper

A small helper for reading player names in Fortnite.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#fortnite_get_player_name)

`fortnite_get_player_name`

Attempts to read and decode a player name from game memory.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `address` Address pointing to a name-related structure in Fortnite.
    

**Returns**

*   The player name as a string on success.
    
*   An empty string `""` if:
    
    *   The process is invalid,
        
    *   The memory cannot be read safely,
        
    *   The decoded name is empty.
        
    

**Example**

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#rust-helper)

Rust Helper

A helper for getting world-space transform positions in Rust (Unity).

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#rust_get_transform_position)

`rust_get_transform_position`

Resolves the world-space position of a Unity transform hierarchy used by Rust.

**Parameters**

*   `proc` Process object.
    
*   `address` Address of a transform-related structure for a given entity.
    

**Returns**

*   On success: three numbers `x, y, z` (Lua returns them as multiple values).
    
*   On failure (invalid process, invalid address, or any internal error): `0, 0, 0`.
    

**Example**

[PreviousWin APIchevron-left](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/win-api)
[NextJson APIchevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/json-api)

Last updated 2 months ago

*   [Unreal Engine Helpers (unreal\_engine)](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#unreal-engine-helpers-unreal_engine)
    
*   [Fortnite Helper](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#fortnite-helper)
    
*   [Rust Helper](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine-specific-api#rust-helper)
    

Copy

    unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info(proc, view_info_address) -> table

Copy

    {
      location = { x = number, y = number, z = number },
      rotation = { pitch = number, yaw = number, roll = number },
      fov      = number
    }

Copy

    local view = unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info(proc, camera_addr)
    
    if view.fov then
        local s = unreal_engine.world_to_screen({ x = 0, y = 0, z = 200 }, view)
        -- ...
    end

Copy

    unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64(proc, view_info_address) -> table

Copy

    {
      location = { x = number, y = number, z = number },
      rotation = { pitch = number, yaw = number, roll = number },
      fov      = number
    }

Copy

    -- Example when you know the game uses a double-precision view structure:
    local view = unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info_f64(proc, view_addr)
    local screen = unreal_engine.world_to_screen({ x = 1000, y = 500, z = 150 }, view)

Copy

    unreal_engine.world_to_screen(world_position, view_info) -> table | nil

Copy

    view_info = {
      location = { x, y, z },
      rotation = { pitch, yaw, roll },
      fov      = number
    }

Copy

    {
      x       = number,  -- screen X (pixels)
      y       = number,  -- screen Y (pixels)
      visible = true
    }

Copy

    local view = unreal_engine.read_minimal_view_info(proc, camera_addr)
    
    local pos = { x = enemy.x, y = enemy.y, z = enemy.z + 80 }
    local screen = unreal_engine.world_to_screen(pos, view)
    
    if screen and screen.visible then
        -- draw box, text, etc. at screen.x, screen.y
    end

Copy

    -- Row-major matrix layout (DirectX-style, Source engine, etc.)
    world_to_screen_rowmajor(world_pos, view_matrix, viewport?) -> {x, y, visible} or nil
    --   world_pos:   table {x, y, z} - 3D world position
    --   view_matrix: accepts table with 16 floats (indices 1-16) or matrix4x4
    --   viewport:    optional table {x, y} - screen size (defaults to overlay size)
    --   returns:     table {x, y, visible} or nil if behind camera
    
    -- Transposed/column-major layout (Unity, OpenGL-style)
    world_to_screen_transposed(world_pos, view_matrix, viewport?) -> {x, y, visible} or nil
    --   world_pos:   table {x, y, z} - 3D world position
    --   view_matrix: accepts table with 16 floats (indices 1-16) or matrix4x4
    --   viewport:    optional table {x, y} - screen size (defaults to overlay size)
    --   returns:     table {x, y, visible} or nil if behind camera

Copy

    fortnite_get_player_name(proc, address) -> string

Copy

    local name = fortnite_get_player_name(proc, name_struct_addr)
    
    if name ~= "" then
        print("Player name:", name)
    end

Copy

    rust_get_transform_position(proc, address) -> x, y, z

Copy

    local x, y, z = rust_get_transform_position(proc, transform_addr)
    
    if x ~= 0 or y ~= 0 or z ~= 0 then
        local screen = unreal_engine.world_to_screen({ x = x, y = y, z = z }, view_info)
        if screen and screen.visible then
            -- draw marker on that entity
        end
    end

# System API (CPU & Disassembly) | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The **System API** provides low-level functionality for CPU information, performance timing, and x64 instruction disassembly using **Zydis**. All functions listed here are available globally inside Lua scripts.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#available-functions)

📌 **Available Functions**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#cpu-information)

**CPU Information**

Function

Returns

Description

`cpu_vendor()`

`string`

CPU vendor (e.g. `"AuthenticAMD"` or `"GenuineIntel"`).

`cpu_brand()`

`string`

Human-readable CPU model string.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#timing-functions)

**Timing Functions**

Function

Returns

Description

`rdtsc()`

`uint64`

Raw timestamp counter from the CPU. Fast but CPU-frequency dependent.

`perf_time()`

`int64`

High-resolution performance counter ticks from Windows.

`perf_frequency()`

`int64`

Number of performance counter ticks per second.

Useful for accurate microbenchmarking:

Copy

    seconds = (perf_time_end - perf_time_start) / perf_frequency()

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#disassembly-zydis)

**Disassembly (Zydis)**

Function

Returns

Description

`zydis_disasm(bytes_table, [runtime_rip])`

`table` (array of instructions)

Disassembles multiple x64 instructions and returns detailed structured output.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly#instruction-structure)

Copy

    {
        runtime_address       = 0x140000000,  -- uint64
        length                = 5,            -- bytes
        mnemonic              = "mov",        -- "push", "call", etc.
        text                  = "mov rbp, rsp",  -- full Intel syntax
        operand_count         = 3,            -- total (explicit + hidden)
        operand_count_visible = 2,            -- explicit operands only
    
        operands = { operand_t, operand_t, ... }
    }

Copy

    {
        id         = 0,
        visibility = "explicit", -- "explicit" | "implicit" | "hidden"
        type       = "reg",      -- "reg" | "mem" | "imm" | "ptr" | "unused"
        size       = 64,         -- bits
    
        -- Register operand
        reg = {
            name = "rbp"
        },
    
        -- Memory operand
        mem = {
            segment          = "ss",
            base             = "rsp",
            index            = nil,
            scale            = 1,
            has_displacement = true,
            displacement     = -0x20,
        },
    
        -- Immediate operand
        imm = {
            is_signed        = true,
            is_relative      = false,
            value            = 48,
            absolute_address = nil, -- if relative & resolvable
        },
    
        -- Pointer operand
        ptr = {
            segment = 0x1234,
            offset  = 0xABCDEF,
        }
    }

Copy

    function main()
        log("CPU Vendor: " .. cpu_vendor())
        log("CPU Brand : " .. cpu_brand())
    end

Copy

    function main()
        local freq = perf_frequency()
        local t0 = perf_time()
    
        -- workload
        for i = 1, 1000000 do end
    
        local t1 = perf_time()
    
        local dt = (t1 - t0) / freq
        log("Elapsed seconds: " .. dt)
    end

Copy

    function main()
        local bytes = {
            0x55,                    -- push rbp
            0x48, 0x89, 0xE5,        -- mov rbp, rsp
            0x48, 0x83, 0xEC, 0x30   -- sub rsp, 0x30
        }
    
        local ins = zydis_disasm(bytes, 0x140000000)
    
        for i, inst in ipairs(ins) do
            log(string.format("0x%X: %s", inst.runtime_address, inst.text))
        end
    end

Copy

    function main()
        local p = ref_process("notepad.exe")
        if not p then return end
    
        local base = p:base_address()
        local bytes = p:rvm(base, 32)
    
        local ins = zydis_disasm(bytes, base)
    
        for _, inst in ipairs(ins) do
            log(inst.runtime_address .. ": " .. inst.text)
        end
    
        deref_process(p)
    end

Copy

    0x140000000: push rbp
      mnemonic = push, length = 1, operands = 1/3
        op1: id=0 type=reg vis=explicit size=64
          reg: rbp
        op2: id=1 type=reg vis=hidden size=64
          reg: rsp
        op3: id=2 type=mem vis=hidden size=64
          mem: seg=ss base=rsp index=nil scale=0 has_disp=false disp=nil
    
    0x140000001: mov rbp, rsp
      mnemonic = mov, length = 3, operands = 2/2
    
    0x140000004: sub rsp, 0x30
      mnemonic = sub, length = 4, operands = 2/3

Copy

    local dt = get_datetime()
    -- dt = {
    --     year        = 2025,
    --     month       = 11,
    --     day         = 27,
    --     hour        = 14,        -- 24h clock
    --     minute      = 5,
    --     second      = 33,
    --     msec        = 120,
    --
    --     day_name    = "Thursday",
    --     month_name  = "November",
    --
    --     hour12      = 2,         -- 12h clock
    --     ampm        = "PM"
    -- }

Copy

    local ts = get_timestamp()
    -- example: 1732734005

Copy

    function main()
        local dt = get_datetime()
    
        log(string.format(
            "Today is %s, %s %d, %d",
            dt.day_name, dt.month_name, dt.day, dt.year
        ))
    
        log(string.format(
            "Local Time: %d:%02d %s",
            dt.hour12, dt.minute, dt.ampm
        ))
    
        local ts = get_timestamp()
        log("Unix Timestamp: " .. ts)
    end

# Render API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#constants)

Constants

Copy

    RR_TOP_LEFT
    RR_TOP_RIGHT
    RR_BOTTOM_LEFT
    RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT

Rectangle corner rounding flags (bitmask), used with `rounding_flags` in rect functions.

Copy

    TE_NONE
    TE_OUTLINE
    TE_SHADOW
    TE_GLOW

Text effects used by `draw_text`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#viewport)

Viewport

Copy

    w, h = get_view()
    scale = get_view_scale()
    fps = get_fps()

*   `get_view()` — returns the current viewport width and height in pixels.
    
*   `get_view_scale()` — returns a reference scale factor (useful for DPI-aware sizes).
    
*   `get_fps()`
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#shapes)

Shapes

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#rectangle-outline)

Rectangle (outline)

Draws a rounded rectangle outline.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#rectangle-filled)

Rectangle (filled)

Draws a filled rounded rectangle.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#line)

Line

Draws a line from `(x1, y1)` to `(x2, y2)`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#arc)

Arc

Draws an arc or pie-slice centered at `(cx, cy)`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#circle)

Circle

Draws a circle centered at `(cx, cy)`.

*   If `filled == true`, draws a filled circle.
    
*   Otherwise draws an outlined circle.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#triangle)

Triangle

Draws a triangle using the three points `(ax, ay)`, `(bx, by)`, `(cx, cy)`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#polygon)

Polygon

*   `xy_pairs` — Lua table of floats: `{ x1, y1, x2, y2, x3, y3, ... }`.
    
*   `count_pairs` — optional; if `nil` or `0`, uses the whole table.
    

Draws a polyline or filled polygon.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#four-corner-gradient)

Four-Corner Gradient

Draws a rectangle with independent colors per corner:

*   top-left: `(tlr, tlg, tlb, tla)`
    
*   top-right: `(trr, trg, trb, tra)`
    
*   bottom-left: `(blr, blg, blb, bla)`
    
*   bottom-right: `(brr, brg, brb, bra)`
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#bitmaps)

Bitmaps

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#create-bitmap)

Create bitmap

*   `data` — Lua table of `uint8` values (byte buffer).
    
*   Returns a handle `bmp` that can be passed to `draw_bitmap`.
    
*   Returns `0` on failure.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#draw-bitmap)

Draw bitmap

Draws a bitmap tinted with color `(r, g, b, a)`.

*   `bmp` — handle returned by `create_bitmap`.
    
*   `rounded` — if `true`, draws with rounded corners.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#fonts-and-text)

Fonts & Text

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#built-in-fonts)

Built-in fonts

Returns a handle to a default font at a given size.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#create-font-from-file)

Create font from file

*   `path` — filesystem path or font name.
    
*   `size` — font size in pixels.
    
*   `anti_aliased` — `true` for smooth text, `false` for pixel-style rendering (boolean).
    
*   `load_color` — `true` to enable color glyphs (emoji / color fonts), `false` for standard monochrome glyphs (boolean).
    
*   `glyph_ranges` — array of custom glyph ranges
    
*   Returns a font handle or `0` on failure.
    

The function searches for fonts inside the API directory (e.g. `verdana_custom.ttf`, `fonts/verdana_custom.ttf`) and may fall back to system font locations. If a font name matches a system font, that one may be loaded instead— use unique names to prevent conflicts.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#create-font-from-memory)

Create font from memory

*   `label` — name/tag for the font (string).
    
*   `size` — font size in pixels.
    
*   `buf` — Lua table of `uint8` values (font binary data).
    
*   `anti_aliased` — `true` for smooth text, `false` for pixel-style rendering (boolean).
    
*   `load_color` — `true` to enable color glyphs (emoji / color fonts), `false` for standard monochrome glyphs (boolean).
    
*   `glyph_ranges` — array of custom glyph ranges
    
*   Returns a font handle or `0` on failure.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#using-custom-glyph-ranges)

Using custom glyph ranges

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#draw-text)

Draw text

*   `text` — string to draw.
    
*   `(r, g, b, a)` — text color.
    
*   `font` — font handle.
    
*   `effect` — one of `TE_NONE`, `TE_OUTLINE`, `TE_SHADOW`, `TE_GLOW`.
    
*   `(er, eg, eb, ea)` — effect color (e.g. shadow/outline color).
    
*   `effect_amount` — intensity scalar.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#text-metrics)

Text metrics

*   `get_text_size` — returns width/height of the rendered `text`.
    
*   `get_char_advance` — returns advance width for a single character (`wchar32`).
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#clipping)

Clipping

*   `clip_push` — pushes a rectangular clip region.
    
*   `clip_pop` — restores the previous clip region.
    

All drawing while a clip is active is restricted to the specified rectangle.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#example)

Example

This draws a centered rounded panel and a title text using the Lua Render API.

[PreviousEnginechevron-left](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/engine)
[NextInput APIchevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/input-api)

Last updated 2 months ago

*   [Constants](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#constants)

*   [Example](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/render-api#example)
    

Copy

    draw_rect(x, y, w, h,
              r, g, b, a,
              thickness, rounding, rounding_flags)

Copy

                     r, g, b, a,
                     rounding, rounding_flags)

Copy

              r, g, b, a,
              thickness)

Copy

             start_angle_deg, sweep_angle_deg,
             r, g, b, a,
             thickness, filled)

Copy

                r, g, b, a,
                thickness, filled)

Copy

                  r, g, b, a,
                  thickness, filled)

Copy

                 r, g, b, a,
                 thickness, filled)

Copy

    draw_four_corner_gradient(x, y, w, h,
                              tlr, tlg, tlb, tla,
                              trr, trg, trb, tra,
                              blr, blg, blb, bla,
                              brr, brg, brb, bra,
                              rounding)

Copy

    bmp = create_bitmap(data)

Copy

    draw_bitmap(bmp, x, y, w, h,
                r, g, b, a,
                rounded)

Copy

    font = get_font18()
    font = get_font20()
    font = get_font24()
    font = get_font28()

Copy

    font = create_font(path, size, anti_aliased, load_color, optional:glyph_ranges)

Copy

    font = create_font_mem(label, size, buf , anti_aliased, load_color, optional:glyph_ranges)

Copy

    local ranges = {
        0x0020, 0x00FF,   -- Basic Latin + Latin-1 Supplement
        0x0400, 0x04FF,   -- Cyrillic
        0
    }
    local font2 = create_font("Arial", 16.0, true, false, ranges)

Copy

    draw_text(text, x, y,
              r, g, b, a,
              font, effect,
              er, eg, eb, ea,
              effect_amount)

Copy

    w, h = get_text_size(font, text,
                         maxw, maxh)
    
    advance = get_char_advance(font, wchar32)

Copy

    clip_push(x, y, w, h)
    clip_pop()

Copy

    local font = 0
    local t = 0
    
    function main()
        log("Lua render example loaded.")
    
        -- Use built-in default font
        font = get_font20()
    
        return 1 -- keep script running
    end
    
    function on_frame()
        -- Get viewport
        local vw, vh = get_view()
        local scale  = get_view_scale()
    
        t = t + 1
    
        -- Panel size
        local w  = 260 * scale
        local h  = 120 * scale
        local cx = vw * 0.5
        local cy = vh * 0.5
        local x  = cx - w * 0.5
        local y  = cy - h * 0.5
    
        -- Background panel
        draw_rect_filled(
            x, y, w, h,
            30, 30, 40, 230,      -- r,g,b,a
            8.0 * scale,          -- rounding
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
        )
    
        -- Outline
        draw_rect(
            x, y, w, h,
            80, 140, 255, 255,    -- r,g,b,a
            2.0 * scale,          -- thickness
            8.0 * scale,          -- rounding
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT | RR_BOTTOM_LEFT | RR_BOTTOM_RIGHT
        )
    
        -- Animated accent bar
        local bar_h = 4 * scale
        draw_rect_filled(
            x, y - bar_h - 2 * scale, w, bar_h,
            120 + (t % 60), 80, 220, 255,
            2.0 * scale,
            RR_TOP_LEFT | RR_TOP_RIGHT
        )
    
        -- Text
        local title = "Lua Render API"
        local w_text, h_text = get_text_size(font, title, 1000, 1000)
    
        local tx = cx - w_text * 0.5
        local ty = cy - h_text * 0.5 - 10 * scale
    
        draw_text(
            title,
            tx, ty,
            255, 255, 255, 255,  -- text color
            font,
            TE_SHADOW,           -- effect
            0, 0, 0, 180,        -- effect color (shadow)
            1.0,                 -- effect amount
        )
    
        -- Subtitle
        local subtitle = "drawing from Lua 5.4.6"
        local sw, sh = get_text_size(font, subtitle, 1000, 1000)
        local sx = cx - sw * 0.5
        local sy = ty + h_text + 8 * scale
    
        draw_text(
            subtitle,
            sx, sy,
            180, 200, 255, 255,
            font,
            TE_NONE,
            0, 0, 0, 0,
            0.0
        )
    end
    
    function on_unload()
        log("Lua render example unloading.")
    end

# Extended Math API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API provides vectors, quaternions, matrices, math constants, and helper functions found in modern game engines.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#contents)

📘 Contents


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Math Constants
    
*   Global Math Helpers
    
*   vector2
    
*   vector3
    
*   quaternion
    
*   matrix4x4
    
*   mat4 Namespace
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#math-constants)

🔢 **Math Constants**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These are available globally:

Name

Value

`M_PI`

3.141592653589793

`M_TAU`

6.283185307179586 (2π)

`M_PI_2`

π/2

`M_PI_4`

π/4

`DEG2RAD`

π/180

`RAD2DEG`

180/π

`PI_OVER_180`

π/180

`INV_PI_OVER_180`

180/π

`M_ZERO`

0

`M_ONE`

1

`M_EPSILON`

0.000001

Usage:

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#global-math-helpers)

🛠 **Global Math Helpers**


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#clamp-x-min-max)

✔ clamp(x, min, max)

Clamps a value between two bounds.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#saturate-x)

✔ saturate(x)

Clamps value to `[0,1]`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#sign-x)

✔ sign(x)

Returns `-1`, `0`, or `1`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#round-x-round_up-x-round_down-x)

✔ round(x), round\_up(x), round\_down(x)

Standard rounding helpers.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#fract-x)

✔ fract(x)

Fractional part (always 0–1, even for negatives).

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#wrap-x-min-max)

✔ wrap(x, min, max)

Wraps a number into a cyclic range.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#lerp-a-b-t)

✔ lerp(a, b, t)

Linear interpolation.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#inverse_lerp-a-b-v)

✔ inverse\_lerp(a, b, v)

Inverse of `lerp`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#remap-a1-b1-a2-b2-v)

✔ remap(a1, b1, a2, b2, v)

Maps a value from one range to another.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#smoothstep-edge0-edge1-x)

✔ smoothstep(edge0, edge1, x)

Smooth Hermite interpolation.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#step-edge-x)

✔ step(edge, x)

Returns 0 if x < edge, else 1.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/extended-math-api#is_nan-x-is_inf-x)

✔ is\_nan(x), is\_inf(x)

Checks numeric state.

Copy

    local t = inverse_lerp(0, 100, 25)   -- 0.25
    local v = remap(0, 1, -1, 1, t)      -- -0.5

Copy

    log("=========== MATH HELPERS TESTS START ===========")
    
    local function approx(a,b,eps)
        eps = eps or 0.000001
        return math.abs(a-b) <= eps
    end
    
    local function assert_eq(a,b,msg)
        if a ~= b then
            log("[ASSERT FAIL] "..msg.." | expected="..tostring(b).." got="..tostring(a))
        else
            log("[PASS] "..msg)
        end
    end
    
    local function assert_approx(a,b,msg)
        if approx(a,b) then
            log("[PASS] "..msg)
        else
            log("[ASSERT FAIL] "..msg.." | expected="..tostring(b).." got="..tostring(a))
        end
    end
    
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    -- clamp(x, min, max)
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    assert_approx(clamp(-1, 0, 1), 0,   "clamp below")
    assert_approx(clamp(0.5, 0, 1), 0.5,"clamp inside")
    assert_approx(clamp(2, 0, 1), 1,    "clamp above")
    -- swapped min/max should still work
    assert_approx(clamp(5, 10, 0), 5,   "clamp swapped bounds")
    
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    -- saturate(x) -> [0,1]
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    assert_approx(saturate(-1), 0,      "saturate below")
    assert_approx(saturate(0.3), 0.3,   "saturate inside")
    assert_approx(saturate(5), 1,       "saturate above")
    
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    -- sign(x)
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    assert_eq(sign( 5),  1,  "sign positive")
    assert_eq(sign(-2), -1,  "sign negative")
    assert_eq(sign( 0),  0,  "sign zero")
    
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    -- round, round_up, round_down
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    assert_approx(round(2.3),  2,   "round 2.3")
    assert_approx(round(2.5),  3,   "round 2.5")
    assert_approx(round(-2.3), -2,  "round -2.3")
    assert_approx(round(-2.5), -3,  "round -2.5")
    
    assert_approx(round_up(2.1),   3, "round_up 2.1")
    assert_approx(round_up(-2.1), -2, "round_up -2.1")
    
    assert_approx(round_down(2.9),   2, "round_down 2.9")
    assert_approx(round_down(-2.1), -3, "round_down -2.1")
    
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    -- fract(x)
    ----------------------------------------------------------------
    assert_approx(fract(1.25), 0.25, "fract 1.25")
    -- our implementation keeps negative fractional part in [0,1)\
    assert_approx(fract(-1.25), 0.75, "fract -1.25")\
    \
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    -- wrap(x, min, max)\
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    assert_approx(wrap(5, 0, 4), 1,   "wrap 5 in [0,4]")\
    assert_approx(wrap(-1, 0, 4), 3,  "wrap -1 in [0,4]")\
    assert_approx(wrap(9, 2, 6), 5, "wrap 9 in [2,6]")\
    assert_approx(wrap(2, 2, 6), 2,   "wrap 2 (edge)")\
    \
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    -- lerp / inverse_lerp\
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    assert_approx(lerp(0, 10, 0.0), 0,   "lerp t=0")\
    assert_approx(lerp(0, 10, 1.0), 10,  "lerp t=1")\
    assert_approx(lerp(0, 10, 0.25), 2.5,"lerp t=0.25")\
    \
    assert_approx(inverse_lerp(0, 10, 2.5), 0.25, "inverse_lerp 2.5 in [0,10]")\
    assert_approx(inverse_lerp(0, 10, 0),    0.0, "inverse_lerp 0")\
    assert_approx(inverse_lerp(0, 10, 10),   1.0, "inverse_lerp 10")\
    \
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    -- remap(a1,b1,a2,b2,v)\
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    assert_approx(remap(0, 10, 0, 100, 2.5), 25,  "remap 2.5 [0,10]->[0,100]")\
    assert_approx(remap(0, 1, -1, 1, 0.5),   0,   "remap 0.5 [0,1]->[-1,1]")\
    assert_approx(remap(-1, 1, 0, 1, 0),     0.5, "remap 0 [-1,1]->[0,1]")\
    \
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    -- smoothstep(edge0,edge1,x)\
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    assert_approx(smoothstep(0,1, -0.5), 0.0,  "smoothstep below")\
    assert_approx(smoothstep(0,1,  0.0), 0.0,  "smoothstep 0")\
    assert_approx(smoothstep(0,1,  1.0), 1.0,  "smoothstep 1")\
    -- at x=0.5 we expect 0.5 for 3t^2-2t^3\
    local s05 = smoothstep(0,1,0.5)\
    assert_approx(s05, 0.5, "smoothstep 0.5")\
    \
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    -- step(edge, x)\
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    assert_approx(step(0.5, 0.3), 0.0, "step below")\
    assert_approx(step(0.5, 0.5), 1.0, "step equal")\
    assert_approx(step(0.5, 0.9), 1.0, "step above")\
    \
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    -- is_nan / is_inf\
    ----------------------------------------------------------------\
    local nan = 0/0\
    local pinf = 1/0\
    local ninf = -1/0\
    \
    assert_eq(is_nan(nan), true,  "is_nan on NaN")\
    assert_eq(is_nan(0),   false, "is_nan on 0")\
    \
    assert_eq(is_inf(pinf), true,  "is_inf +inf")\
    assert_eq(is_inf(ninf), true,  "is_inf -inf")\
    assert_eq(is_inf(123),  false, "is_inf 123")\
    \
    log("=========== MATH HELPERS TESTS END ===========")\
    \
    function main()\
        return 1;\
    end

# CS2 Extended API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API is available in both the Uni API and the CS2 product.

In the CS2 product, all standard Proc API functions are supported **except**:

*   Process referencing by PID/name
    
*   Engine-specific helpers
    
*   Virtual memory allocation (`alloc_vm` / `free_vm`)
    

On CS2 Product, `ref_process()` always returns the **CS2 process only**, so it is used like:

Copy

    local cs2 = ref_process()  -- for CS2 Product only

There is **no memory allocation API** exposed in the CS2 product.

* * *

**🔗** `**process:cs2_get_interface(module_base, name)**`

Resolves a **CreateInterface-style** interface exported by a CS2 module.

Copy

    addr = process:cs2_get_interface(module_base, name)

**Parameters**

*   `module_base` Base address of the module that exports `CreateInterface`, e.g.:
    
    *   `"tier0.dll"`
        
    
    Typically obtained via:
    
    Copy
    
        local base, size = process:get_module("tier0.dll")
    
*   `name` Interface name string, e.g.:
    
    *   `"VEngineCvar007"`
        
    

**Returns**

*   Absolute pointer to the resolved interface (Lua integer).
    
*   `0` if the interface cannot be found or the arguments are invalid.
    

* * *

**🧬** `**process:cs2_get_schema_dump()**`

Dumps all Schema System fields for `client.dll` via `schemasystem.dll`.

**Return value**

A **Lua array-style table** (`1..N`) where each element is a table:

**Fields**

*   `name` — `"ClassName::fieldName"`, UTF-8 string e.g. `"CPulse_CallInfo::m_nEditorNodeID"`, `"C_BaseEntity::m_iHealth"`
    
*   `offset` — field offset from the base of that class.
    

If no schema data can be read, returns an **empty table**.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/cs2-extended-api#example-interface-lookup--schema-dump-lua)

🧪 Example – Interface Lookup + Schema Dump (Lua)

[PreviousSound APIchevron-left](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/sound-api)
[NextOtherschevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/others)

Last updated 2 months ago

Copy

    entries = process:cs2_get_schema_dump()

Copy

    {
        name   = "ClassName::fieldName", -- string
        offset = 0x10,                   -- integer offset
    }

Copy

    local function dump_schema(proc)
        local entries = proc:cs2_get_schema_dump()
        if not entries or #entries == 0 then
            log("[LUA] schema dump empty")
            return
        end
    
        log("[LUA] Dumping " .. #entries .. " schema fields...")
    
        for i = 1, #entries do
            local e = entries[i]
            if e then
                -- format: CPulse_CallInfo::m_nEditorNodeID @ 0x00000010
                log(string.format(
                    "%s @ 0x%08X",
                    e.name,
                    e.offset
                ))
            end
        end
    
        log("[LUA] Schema dump complete.")
    end
    
    function main()
        -- Uni API build:
        local cs2 = ref_process("cs2.exe")
    
        -- On the CS2 Product build, just use:
        --   local cs2 = ref_process()
    
        if not cs2 or not cs2:alive() then
            log("[LUA] cs2.exe not found")
            return 0
        end
    
        local tierBase, tierSize = cs2:get_module("tier0.dll")
        if not tierBase then
            log("[LUA] tier0.dll not found")
            return 0
        end
    
        local iface = cs2:cs2_get_interface(tierBase, "VEngineCvar007")
        if iface == 0 then
            log("[LUA] interface not found!")
            return 0
        end
    
        log(string.format(
            "VEngineCvar007 interface at 0x%016X",
            iface
        ))
    
        dump_schema(cs2)
        return 1
    end

---

# Overview | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This environment provides a lightweight scripting layer for UI, rendering, memory analysis and interaction in Perception.cx. It uses **AngelScript** with core add-ons and PCX-specific APIs enabled by default.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview#core-add-ons)

Core Add-ons

The following standard AngelScript modules are registered:

*   **string** — native string support.
    
*   **array** — dynamic arrays with value semantics.
    
*   **dictionary** — key/value associative maps.
    
*   **math** — standard math utilities.
    
*   **any** — variant type for mixed data.
    
*   **grid** — 2D grid storage type.
    
*   **script helper** — Exception helper functions
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/overview#pcx-addons)

PCX Addons

Custom host APIs extend the scripting environment:

*   **Unicorn** — A CPU Emulator
    
*   **Atomic Types** — thread-safe lock-free integer primitives
    
*   **Render API** — draw shapes, text, images, and gradients, now advance gpu math + advance functions.
    
*   **Input API** — mouse, keyboard, and scroll input
    
*   **Host Utilities** — logging and script lifecycle helpers
    
*   **Proc API** — memory inspection and manipulation
    
*   **Mutex API** — thread-safety primitives for synchronized access
    
*   **GUI API** — create and interact with UI elements
    
*   **System API** — CPU info, instruction utilities, disassembly
    
*   **Net API** — HTTP, HTTPS, and WebSocket networking
    
*   **File System API** — read, write, and manage files/folders
    
*   **Extended Math API** — vectors, matrices, quaternions, and math helpers
    
*   **Engine Specific API** — read engine specific structures easier
    
*   **Json API** — JSON parsing and serialization utilities for AngelScript dictionaries
    
*   **Utilities** — encoding, decoding, etc
    
*   **Zydis Encoder** — Assemble x86/x64 instructions into machine code bytes
    
*   **Intrinsics** — Intrinsics (SSE / Bit Operations)
    
*   **Sound API**
    
*   **Bit Reinterpret Helpers** — convert values by reinterpreting their underlying bit patterns
    
*   **CS2 Extended API** \- For Official CS2 Product
    

[PreviousOtherschevron-left](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/others)

# Utilities | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The `util` module provides fast Base64, Hex, and URL encoding/decoding helpers for Lua scripts.

All functions operate on **raw byte strings**, not UTF-8 text, so they safely support:

*   Binary data
    
*   Network packets
    
*   Ciphertext
    
*   Hashes
    
*   Buffers containing `\0` bytes
    
*   Arbitrary byte sequences
    

The module is registered globally as:

Copy

    util = {
        base64_encode = function(str) end,
        base64_decode = function(str) end,
        hex_encode    = function(str) end,
        hex_decode    = function(str) end,
        url_encode    = function(str) end,
        url_decode    = function(str) end,
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#url-encode-decode)

URL Encode / Decode


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Matches standard percent-encoding:

*   Safe characters stay as-is: `A–Z a–z 0–9 - _ . ~`
    
*   Everything else becomes `%XX`
    

`+` is **not** treated as space. Binary bytes are preserved.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#util.url_encode-str)

`util.url_encode(str)`

Encodes text for safe URL usage.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#example-4)

Example

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#util.url_decode-str)

`util.url_decode(str)`

Decodes `%XX` sequences back into bytes.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#example-5)

Example

Invalid `%` sequences are returned literally.

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#binary-safety)

Binary Safety


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All `util.*` functions:

*   correctly handle `\0` bytes
    
*   accept arbitrary binary input
    
*   never corrupt data
    
*   do not assume UTF-8
    
*   support large buffers
    

Tested with byte sizes from 1 → 256 without corruption.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#summary)

Summary


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Function

Description

`util.base64_encode(str)`

Encode bytes → Base64

`util.base64_decode(str)`

Decode Base64 → bytes (or nil+error)

`util.hex_encode(str)`

Encode bytes → uppercase hex

`util.hex_decode(str)`

Decode hex → bytes (or nil+error)

`util.url_encode(str)`

Percent-encode unsafe characters

`util.url_decode(str)`

Decode `%XX` → bytes

*   [URL Encode / Decode](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/utilities#url-encode-decode)

Copy

    local out = util.base64_encode("hello")
    print(out)   --> aGVsbG8=

Copy

    local raw, err = util.base64_decode("aGVsbG8=")
    if raw then
        print(raw)   --> hello
    else
        print("Decode failed:", err)
    end

Copy

    local v, err = util.base64_decode("!!!!bad!!!!")
    -- v   == nil
    -- err == "Invalid base64 character"

Copy

    local out = util.hex_encode("ABC")
    print(out)   --> 414243

Copy

    local raw = util.hex_decode("414243")
    print(raw)   --> ABC

Copy

    util.hex_decode("ABC")
    -- nil, "Hex string length must be even"
    
    util.hex_decode("GGGG")
    -- nil, "Invalid hex character"

Copy

    local enc = util.url_encode("hello world! 100% ok?")
    print(enc)
    -- "hello%20world%21%20100%25%20ok%3F"

Copy

    local dec = util.url_decode("name=John%20Doe&msg=hi%21")
    print(dec)
    -- "name=John Doe&msg=hi!"

Copy

    local original = "hello world"
    local enc = util.base64_encode(original)
    local dec = util.base64_decode(enc)
    assert(dec == original)

Copy

    local original = "hello world"
    local hex = util.hex_encode(original)
    local raw = util.hex_decode(hex)
    assert(raw == original)

Copy

    local original = "[email protected]&msg=hello!"
    local enc = util.url_encode(original)
    local dec = util.url_decode(enc)
    assert(dec == original)
