# Bit Reinterpret Helpers | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The **Bit Reinterpret Helpers** allow scripts to inspect the raw bit-pattern of numeric values by converting them into a `uint32`.

These functions **do not convert or scale values** — they reinterpret the raw memory bits of the input

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-f_to_u32-float-f)

`uint32 f_to_u32(float f)`

Returns the raw 32-bit IEEE-754 representation of a float.

Copy

    uint32 bits = f_to_u32(1.0f);     // 0x3F800000

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-u8_to_u32-uint8-v)

`uint32 u8_to_u32(uint8 v)`

Reinterprets a `uint8` as a `uint32`.

Copy

    uint32 bits = u8_to_u32(255);     // 0x000000FF

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-u16_to_u32-uint16-v)

`uint32 u16_to_u32(uint16 v)`

Reinterprets the lower 16 bits of a `uint16` as a 32-bit integer.

Copy

    uint32 bits = u16_to_u32(50000);

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-u64_to_u32-uint64-v)

`uint32 u64_to_u32(uint64 v)`

Returns the **lower 32 bits** of a 64-bit unsigned integer.

Copy

    uint32 bits = u64_to_u32(0x1122334455667788);

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i8_to_u32-int8-v)

`uint32 i8_to_u32(int8 v)`

Reinterprets a signed 8-bit integer as a 32-bit unsigned integer.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i16_to_u32-int16-v)

`uint32 i16_to_u32(int16 v)`

Reinterprets a signed 16-bit integer as 32 bits.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i32_to_u32-int32-v)

`uint32 i32_to_u32(int32 v)`

Reinterprets a signed 32-bit integer as an unsigned one **without numerical conversion**.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-i64_to_u32-int64-v)

`uint32 i64_to_u32(int64 v)`

Returns the lower 32 bits of a 64-bit signed integer.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint32-d_to_u32-double-v)

`uint32 d_to_u32(double v)`

Returns the first 4 bytes of a 64-bit double (the lower half of the binary representation).

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#float-bits_to_float-uint-raw)

`**float bits_to_float(uint raw)**`

Reinterprets a 32-bit unsigned integer as an IEEE-754 `float`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#double-bits_to_double-uint64-raw)

`**double bits_to_double(uint64 raw)**`

Reinterprets a 64-bit unsigned integer as an IEEE-754 `double`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint-float_to_bits-float-value)

`**uint float_to_bits(float value)**`

Returns the exact 32-bit IEEE-754 bit pattern of a `float`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#uint64-double_to_bits-double-value)

`**uint64 double_to_bits(double value)**`

Returns the exact 64-bit IEEE-754 bit pattern of a `double`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/bit-reinterpret-helpers#float-u32_to_f-uint-raw)

`**float u32_to_f(uint raw)**`

Convenience alias for `bits_to_float(raw)`.

[PreviousSound APIchevron-left](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/sound-api)
[NextCS2 Extended APIchevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/cs2-extended-api)

Last updated 4 months ago

Copy

    uint32 bits = i8_to_u32(-5);      // 0xFFFFFFFB

Copy

    uint32 bits = i16_to_u32(-1234);

Copy

    uint32 bits = i32_to_u32(-1);     // 0xFFFFFFFF

Copy

    uint32 bits = i64_to_u32(-1);     // 0xFFFFFFFF

Copy

    uint32 bits = d_to_u32(3.1415926535);

Copy

    float f = bits_to_float(0x3F800000);    // 1.0f

Copy

    double d = bits_to_double(0x400921FB54442D18);   // 3.141592653589793

Copy

    uint bits = float_to_bits(1.0f);        // 0x3F800000

Copy

    uint64 bits = double_to_bits(3.141592653589793); // 0x400921FB54442D18

Copy

    float f = u32_to_f(0xBF800000);         // -1.0f

# Engine | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#overview)

⚙️ Overview

A callback is a **script function** that executes repeatedly on a background thread created by the engine. Each callback receives a unique **callback ID** (integer) and runs at a defined interval in milliseconds.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#registration-functions)

🧩 Registration Functions

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#register-callback)

Register Callback

Copy

    int register_callback(const __Internal_CallbackFn@ fn, int every_ms, int data_index, bool render_on_top = false)

Registers a new recurring callback function. The engine launches a lightweight thread that periodically invokes your callback, passing both its unique ID and the `data_index` you supplied.

**Parameter**

**Type**

**Description**

`fn`

`__Internal_CallbackFn@`

Function pointer to the callback (takes two integer arguments — the callback ID and the data index).

`every_ms`

`int`

Delay in milliseconds between callback executions.

`data_index`

`int`

User-defined integer value forwarded to your callback each time it runs. This can represent a dataset slot, UI layer, or logic group.

`render_on_top`

`bool`

Optional flag. Set to `true` to render this callback’s output above everything else. If multiple callbacks use this, registration order still determines which one is topmost. Defaults to `false`.

**Returns:** A unique callback ID (`int`) if successful, or `0` on failure. Drawing And Input is unique for each thread.

> 🧠 The callback executes in its own thread. Each iteration:
> 
> 1.  Begins input collection
>     
> 2.  Executes your callback function
>     
> 3.  Submits the current draw list
>     
> 4.  Ends input and sleeps for `every_ms`
>     

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#unregister-callback)

Unregister Callback

Stops a previously registered callback and terminates its thread.

Parameter

Type

Description

id

int

The callback ID returned by `register_callback`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#callback-function-type)

🧠 Callback Function Type

The callback function type is defined internally by the engine:

Your script callback must accept **two integer parameters**:

**Parameter**

**Type**

**Description**

`callback_id`

`int`

The callback ID returned by `register_callback`. This uniquely identifies the running callback instance.

`data_index`

`int`

A user-defined or engine-supplied index value associated with this callback execution. Can be used to differentiate multiple data contexts handled by the same callback.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#example)

Example

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/engine#logging-helper)

🪵 Logging Helper

* * *

get\_username(): string

Returns the current PCX username as a string.

**Syntax**

[NextAtomic Typeschevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/atomic-types)

Copy

    void unregister_callback(int id)

Copy

    funcdef void __Internal_CallbackFn(int callback_id, int data_index)

Copy

    void on_update(int callback_id, int data_index)
    {
        log("Callback " + callback_id + " tick (data=" + data_index + ")");
    
        // draw something using data_index
        float x = 100 + data_index * 40;
        draw_circle(x, 200, 10, 255,200,100,255, 2.0f, false);
    }
    
    int main()
    {
        // Run callback every 50ms
        int cb = register_callback(on_update, 50, 34);
        log("Registered callback " + cb);
    
        return 1; // keep script running
    }

Copy

    void log(const string &in message)
    // Displays a standard informational message in the UI log overlay.
    
    void log_error(const string &in message)
    // Displays an error-styled message in the UI log overlay and raises an exception.
    
    void log_console(const string &in message)
    // Writes a message to the debug console (persistent until the console is cleared).
    
    void log_console_error(const string &in message)
    // Writes an error-styled message to the debug console in red and raises an exception.

Copy

    log("Log Example");
    log_error("Error Log Example");
    log_console("Current HP : 100");
    log_console_error("Error Log Example");

Copy

    float r = 0.0f;
    
    void animate_cursor(int id, int data_index)
    {
        float x, y;
        get_mouse_pos(x, y);
        
        r += 2.0f;
        
        draw_circle(x, y, 12 + sin(r * 0.1f) * 4,
        255, 100, 50, 255,
        2.0f, false);
    }
    
    int main()
    {
        register_callback(animate_cursor, 1, 0);
        return 1;
    }

# Proc API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API lets scripts inspect and modify the memory of external processes via a `process` userdata. Handles are created with `ref_process(...)` and released with `deref_process(process)`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#process-handles)

🔑 Process Handles

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#userdata-type)

Userdata Type

All functions operate on a `process` userdata created by `ref_process`.

Copy

    -- Get a process handle by PID
    local proc = ref_process(1234)
    
    -- Get a process handle by name
    local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")

If the process is not found, `ref_process` returns `nil`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#referencing-releasing)

Referencing / Releasing

Copy

    process = ref_process(pid_or_name)   -- global
    deref_process(process)               -- global

*   `ref_process(pid)` – `pid` is a number (Windows PID).
    
*   `ref_process("name.exe")` – search by executable name.
    
*   `deref_process(process)` – releases the reference; the userdata becomes invalid.
    
*   You must also call `deref_process` if `process:alive()` returns `false`.
    

> Each Lua script keeps its own list of referenced processes internally. Always call `deref_process(proc)` when you’re done.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#process-info)

🧬 Process Info

*   `base_address()` – Image base address of the process.
    
*   `peb()` – Address of the process’ PEB.
    
*   `pid()` – Process ID.
    
*   `alive()` - Determines whether the process is currently alive and running.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#address-validity)

Address Validity

Check if an address is mapped inside target process.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#scalar-reads)

📖 Scalar Reads

All addresses are **virtual addresses** in the target process.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#unsigned-integers)

Unsigned Integers

Reads unsigned integers from `addr`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#signed-integers)

Signed Integers

Reads signed integers from `addr`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#floating-point)

Floating Point

Reads floating point values from `addr`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#scalar-writes)

✏️ Scalar Writes

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#unsigned-integers-1)

Unsigned Integers

Writes an unsigned integer at `addr`. Returns `true` on success.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#signed-integers-1)

Signed Integers

Writes a signed integer at `addr`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#floating-point-1)

Floating Point

Writes `float` / `double`.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#strings)

🔤 Strings

Read and write null-terminated strings from the remote process.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#read-strings)

Read Strings

*   `rs` – Reads up to `max_chars` characters from `addr`.
    
*   `rws` – Reads a wide string and converts it to a Lua UTF-8 string.
    
*   If nothing valid is read, an empty string is returned.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#write-strings)

Write Strings

*   `ws` – Writes `text` bytes plus a terminating `\0`.
    
*   `wws` – Converts `text` to UTF-16 and writes plus wide `\0`.
    

Returns `true` on success.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#raw-memory-byte-tables)

📦 Raw Memory (byte tables)

Use Lua tables of bytes (`1..N`, values `0–255`) for bulk reads / writes.

*   `rvm` – Returns a new table of length `size` filled with bytes from `addr`.
    
*   `wvm` – Writes all bytes in `byte_table` to `addr`. Returns `true` if all bytes are written.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#simd-helpers)

🧮 SIMD Helpers

Convenience helpers for 16/32/64-byte SIMD vectors (raw bytes).

All values are plain bytes (`0–255`). `wXXX` returns `false` if the table is too short or the write fails.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#modules-and-pattern-scanning)

📦 Modules & Pattern Scanning

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#module-lookup)

Module Lookup

*   `name` – Module name, e.g. `"notepad.exe"`, `"client.dll"`.
    
*   Returns `base, size` on success.
    
*   Returns `nil` if the module is not found.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#code-pattern-scan)

Code Pattern Scan

*   `search_start` – Starting address.
    
*   `search_size` – Number of bytes to scan.
    
*   `signature` – Pattern string, e.g. `"48 8B ?? ?? ?? 89"` (same format as your internal pattern scanner).
    

Returns:

*   `addr` – Address of the first match, or `0` if not found.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#example-scanning-notepad-lua)

🔍 Example: Scanning Notepad (Lua)

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#proc-read_struct)

`proc:read_struct`


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Reads a **single C-style structure** from the target process using a descriptor table.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#signature)

**Signature**

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#parameters)

**Parameters**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#base_address)

`**base_address**`

Absolute address of the struct in the remote process.

####

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#proc-get_all_tebs)

`proc:get_all_tebs()`

Returns a Lua table of **TEB addresses (uint64)** for threads in the target process.

**Syntax**

**Returns**

*   `{ teb1, teb2, ... }` where each `teb` is a **virtual address** in the remote process
    
*   `{}` if none found / enumeration fails
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#virtual-memory-allocation)

Virtual Memory Allocation

These functions let you allocate and manage RWX memory inside the target process. They are intended for advanced use; you are fully responsible for tracking and freeing any allocations you create.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#important-memory-management-notes-must-read)

🔴 Important Memory Management Notes (MUST READ!)

These points are critical for using `alloc_vm` safely:

*   **Control Flow Guard** If the target process has Control Flow Guard (CFG) enabled and you intend to execute code from this region, CFG may block all jumps and calls into the allocated memory. To avoid this, CFG must be fully disabled for the target process. Be aware that disabling CFG reduces the security of the device.
    
*   **Allocations are not automatically freed.** Every allocation you create must be manually released using `free_vm()`. If you lose track of an allocation, the memory will remain reserved until the target process exits.
    
*   **Allocations persist for the lifetime of the target process.** Memory created with `alloc_vm` is automatically released only when the **target process** itself closes.
    
*   **Closing the Perception overlay will clear all allocations.** When the overlay is closed, Perception will clean up every RWX allocation for _all_ processes currently referenced. If you need an allocation to stay alive, **do not close the overlay** while that memory is being used.
    
*   **Repeated unfreed allocations can exhaust physical memory.** If you repeatedly allocate memory without freeing it, these leaks will accumulate and can eventually **consume all available physical RAM**, potentially degrading system performance or causing instability. If you are writing an injector make sure your inject frees the memory
    
*   **If you are writing an injector, you must free allocated memory.** Any injector, loader, or external tool that allocates memory through `alloc_vm` is responsible for freeing it once the memory is no longer needed. Failing to do so will leave permanent physical memory leaks until the target process exits.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#functions)

Functions

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#uint64-proc-alloc_vm-size)

`uint64 proc:alloc_vm(size)`

Allocates a block of **read–write–execute (RWX)** memory inside the target process and returns its base address.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#parameters-2)

Parameters

*   **size** — Size of the allocation in bytes.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#returns-2)

Returns

*   Base address of the allocation on success.
    
*   `0` on failure.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#notes)

Notes

*   Allocated memory is **not tied to any module** and is **not discoverable** through helpers like module queries or pattern scans. You must store and manage the returned address yourself.
    
*   The memory is RWX. If the target process uses **Control Flow Guard (CFG)** and you intend to execute code from this region, CFG may block jumps/calls unless the target allows it.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#bool-proc-free_vm-address)

`bool proc:free_vm(address)`

Frees a region previously allocated with `proc:alloc_vm()`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#parameters-3)

Parameters

*   **address** — The exact base address returned by `alloc_vm`.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#returns-3)

Returns

*   `true` if the region was successfully freed.
    
*   `false` if the address is invalid or the free fails.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#export-lookup-process-get_proc_address)

🔗 Export Lookup – `process:get_proc_address`

Resolves the address of an **exported function or symbol** inside a module in the target process.

*   `module_base` Base address of the module **inside the target process**. Typically obtained from:
    
    *   `process:base_address()`, or
        
    *   `local base, size = process:get_module("module_name.dll")`.
        
    
*   `export_name` Name of the exported function/symbol, e.g. `"Sleep"`, `"CreateFileW"`, `"DllMain"`.
    

**Returns**

*   Absolute **virtual address** of the exported symbol in the target process (as a Lua integer).
    
*   `0` if the export is not found or the arguments are invalid.
    

**Notes**

*   This walks the module’s **export table only** – it does _not_ look at imports or IAT.
    
*   The returned address is suitable for:
    
    *   Remote call stubs / shellcode.
        
    *   Manual thunks that jump directly to an API inside the target module.
        
    

**Example**

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#import-table-iat-slot-lookup-process-get_import_rdata_address)

🧷 Import Table (IAT) Slot Lookup – `process:get_import_rdata_address`

Resolves the **address of the import table entry** (IAT slot) for a given imported function inside a module.

This does **not** return the function’s address itself – it returns the address of the **pointer stored in** `**.rdata**` **/ IAT**. You can then read or patch that pointer for IAT hooks.

*   `module_base` Base address of the module whose imports you want to inspect/patch (usually the main EXE or a specific DLL), e.g. from `process:get_module(...)`.
    
*   `import_name` Name of the imported function (as it appears in the import table), e.g. `"Sleep"`, `"MessageBoxW"`.
    

**Returns**

*   Address of the **IAT entry** (pointer-sized slot) as a Lua integer.
    
*   `0` if the import cannot be found or arguments are invalid.
    

**Typical usage**

*   Read the current imported function pointer:
    
*   Install a simple IAT hook (patch the slot to point to your stub):
    

**Notes**

*   Only sees functions present in the module’s **static import table**.
    
*   Manually resolved APIs (e.g. `GetProcAddress` into some custom region) will **not** show up here.
    
*   Designed for **IAT hooks** and for shellcode that wants to call through the same import slot as the module.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#virtual-memory-analysis)

Virtual Memory Analysis

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#proc-virtual_query-address-greater-than-start-uint64-size-uint64-protection-int-heap_likely-bool-or)

`proc:virtual_query(address) -> (start:uint64, size:uint64, protection:int, heap_likely:bool)|nil`

Queries the virtual memory region containing the given `address`.

**Parameters:**

*   `address` — a `uint64` virtual address.
    

**Returns:**

*   `start` — region base address (`uint64`)
    
*   `size` — region size in bytes (`uint64`)
    
*   `protection` — region protection flags (`int`)
    
*   `heap_likely` — `true` if the region is heuristically likely to be heap/alloc-like (`bool`)
    
*   `nil` if the address is not mapped or cannot be queried.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#proc-get_vad_snapshot-heap_likely_only-bool-greater-than-table)

`proc:get_vad_snapshot(heap_likely_only:bool) -> table`

Builds a snapshot of virtual memory regions.

**Parameters:**

*   `heap_likely_only` — when `true`, only heap-like regions are returned; when `false`, all regions are returned.
    

**Returns:**

A 1-based Lua array of region tables:

Each region table contains:

*   `start` (`uint64`)
    
*   `size` (`uint64`)
    
*   `end` (`uint64`)
    
*   `protection` (`int`)
    
*   `heap_likely` (`bool`)
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#memory-scanning-helpers)

**Memory Scanning Helpers**

These helpers scan the target process memory by iterating over the snapshot of virtual memory regions. All scanning functions return a **1-based Lua table** of matching virtual addresses:

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api#proc-scan_string-text-string-heap_only-bool-or-nil-greater-than-table)

`proc:scan_string(text:string, heap_only:bool|nil) -> table`

Scan for occurrences of an ASCII/multibyte constant string in memory.

*   `text` — the pattern to search for.
    
*   `heap_only` — optional `bool` filter restricting scan to heap-like regions (`false` if nil).

*   `heap_only` — optional `bool` filter.

    process:rws(addr, max_chars) --> string    -- UTF-16 wide -> Lua string

Copy

    process:wws(addr, text) --> bool   -- UTF-16 wide

Copy

    process:rvm(addr, size)          --> { byte1, byte2, ... }
    process:wvm(addr, byte_table)    --> bool

Copy

    process:r128(addr)        --> { b1..b16 }
    process:r256(addr)        --> { b1..b32 }
    process:r512(addr)        --> { b1..b64 }
    
    process:w128(addr, t16)   --> bool  -- t16 length >= 16
    process:w256(addr, t32)   --> bool  -- t32 length >= 32
    process:w512(addr, t64)   --> bool  -- t64 length >= 64

Copy

    local base, size = process:get_module(name)

Copy

    local addr = process:find_code_pattern(search_start, search_size, signature)

Copy

    function main()
        log("==== LUA PROC API TEST START ====")
    
        local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")
        if not proc then
            log("[-] Failed to ref notepad.exe")
            return
        end
    
        local pid   = proc:pid()
        local base  = proc:base_address()
        local peb   = proc:peb()
    
        log(string.format("[+] Referenced Notepad: pid=%d", pid))
        log(string.format("    Base Address = 0x%016X", base))
        log(string.format("    PEB          = 0x%016X", peb))
    
        -- DOS header
        local b0 = proc:ru8(base)
        local b1 = proc:ru8(base + 1)
        log(string.format("Header bytes: %02X %02X", b0, b1))
    
        -- First 16 bytes as hex
        local raw = proc:rvm(base, 16)
        local hex = {}
        for i = 1, #raw do
            hex[#hex+1] = string.format("%02X", raw[i])
        end
        log("DOS header (16 bytes): " .. table.concat(hex, " "))
    
        -- Module + pattern scan
        local mod_base, mod_size = proc:get_module("notepad.exe")
        if mod_base then
            log(string.format("Module Base = 0x%016X", mod_base))
            log(string.format("Module Size = 0x%X",    mod_size))
    
            local addr = proc:find_code_pattern(mod_base, mod_size, "4D 5A")
            log(string.format("Pattern '4D 5A' found at 0x%016X", addr))
        else
            log("[-] get_module('notepad.exe') failed")
        end
    
        -- SIMD round-trip (128-bit)
        local v128 = proc:r128(base)
        local ok = proc:w128(base, v128)
        log("w128 ok? " .. tostring(ok))
    
        deref_process(proc)
        log("==== LUA PROC API TEST END ====")
    end

        offset = <byte offset>,
        type   = "<field type>"

    local t = proc:read_struct(addr, DESC)
    
    print(t.health)
    print(t.pos_x)

Copy

    local DOS_HEADER = {
        e_magic  = { offset = 0x00, type = "u16" },
        e_lfanew = { offset = 0x3C, type = "u32" },
    }
    
    local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")
    local base = proc:get_module("notepad.exe")
    
    local dos = proc:read_struct(base, DOS_HEADER)
    
    log_console(string.format("e_magic  = 0x%04X", dos.e_magic))
    log_console(string.format("e_lfanew = 0x%08X", dos.e_lfanew))

        table descriptor
    )

    local arr = proc:read_struct_array(addr, 10, 0x140, DESC)
    print(arr[1].health)

Copy

    local PLAYER = {
        health = { offset = 0x10, type = "i32" },
        armor  = { offset = 0x14, type = "i32" },
        pos_x  = { offset = 0x30, type = "f32" },
    }
    
    local base = 0x12345678
    local size = 0x140
    local count = 5
    
    local players = proc:read_struct_array(base, count, size, PLAYER)
    
    for i, p in ipairs(players) do
        log_console(string.format(
            "Player %d: hp=%d armor=%d x=%.1f",
            i, p.health, p.armor, p.pos_x
        ))
    end

Copy

    local proc = ref_process("notepad.exe")
    if not proc then return end
    
    local kbase, ksize = proc:get_module("KERNEL32.DLL")
    if kbase then
        local addr_sleep = proc:get_proc_address(kbase, "Sleep")
        log(string.format("Sleep @ 0x%016X", addr_sleep))
    end
    
    deref_process(proc)

Copy

    slot_addr = process:get_import_rdata_address(module_base, import_name)

Copy

    local slot = proc:get_import_rdata_address(mod_base, "Sleep")
    if slot ~= 0 then
        local current = proc:ru64(slot)   -- current function pointer
        log(string.format("IAT[Sleep] = 0x%016X", current))
    end

Copy

    local slot = proc:get_import_rdata_address(mod_base, "Sleep")
    if slot ~= 0 then
        -- 'stub_addr' is an RWX address you allocated with proc:alloc_vm(...)
        local ok = proc:wu64(slot, stub_addr)
        log("IAT hook applied? " .. tostring(ok))
    end

Copy

    {
       { start=<uint64>, size=<uint64>, ["end"]=<uint64>, protection=<int>, heap_likely=<bool> },
       ...
    }

Copy

    { addr1, addr2, ... }

---

# Json API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The AngelScript JSON API provides robust parsing and encoding of JSON directly into native AngelScript structures. JSON objects map to **dictionary** objects, using standard AngelScript types.

This API mirrors the Lua JSON API and is designed to behave identically where possible.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#overview)

Overview

Available functions:

Function

Description

`json_parse(text, result, error)`

Parse JSON text into a `dictionary`

`json_decode(text, result, error)`

Alias of `json_parse`

`json_stringify(value, json, error)`

Convert a `dictionary` into a JSON string

`json_encode(value, json, error)`

Alias of `json_stringify`

All functions return **true on success** and **false on failure**, with detailed error messages.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#json-dictionary)

JSON → Dictionary

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#bool-json_parse-const-string-and-in-text-dictionary-and-out-result-string-and-out-error)

`bool json_parse(const string &in text, dictionary &out result, string &out error)`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#bool-json_decode-const-string-and-in-text-dictionary-and-out-result-string-and-out-error)

`bool json_decode(const string &in text, dictionary &out result, string &out error)`

Parses a JSON string and converts it into a nested AngelScript `dictionary`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#parameters)

Parameters

Name

Type

Description

`text`

`string`

JSON text to parse

`result`

`dictionary`

Output dictionary filled with parsed values

`error`

`string`

Error message if the function fails

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#json-angelscript-type-mapping)

JSON → AngelScript Type Mapping

JSON

AngelScript

Object `{}`

`dictionary` (recursively nested)

String `"text"`

`string`

Number `123`, `4.5`

`double`

Boolean `true/false`

`double` (`1.0`/`0.0`)

null

_field omitted_

Array `[...]`

_(currently skipped)_

`bool json_stringify(const dictionary &in value, string &out json, string &out error)`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#bool-json_encode-const-dictionary-and-in-value-string-and-out-json-string-and-out-error)

`bool json_encode(const dictionary &in value, string &out json, string &out error)`

Converts a dictionary (and any nested dictionaries) into valid JSON text.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#unsupported-types)

Unsupported Types

The AngelScript dictionary can technically store any type, but the JSON stringifier only supports:

*   `double`
    
*   `string`
    
*   `bool`
    
*   `dictionary@`
    

Anything else causes:

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/json-api#arrays)

Arrays

JSON arrays (`[ ... ]`) are **currently skipped**. If you need them, support can be added using `array<T>` or `CScriptArray`.

    if (!ok)
    {
        log_error("JSON parse failed: " + err);
        return;
    }
    
    double a;
    string b;
    
    d.get("a", a);    // 1.0
    d.get("b", b);    // "hello"

    }

    string text = """
    {
        "player": {
            "name": "Alice",
            "pos": { "x": 10, "y": 20 }
        }
    }
    """;
    
    dictionary root;
    string err;
    
    json_parse(text, root, err);
    
    dictionary@ player;
    root.get("player", @player);
    
    string name;
    dictionary@ pos;
    double px, py;
    
    player.get("name", name);
    player.get("pos", @pos);
    pos.get("x", px);
    pos.get("y", py);

Copy

    {"a":1,"b":null,"c":2}

Copy

    d.exists("a") == true
    d.exists("b") == false
    d.exists("c") == true

Copy

    dictionary d;
    d.set("value", 123.0);
    d.set("name", "Test");
    d.set("ok", true);
    
    dictionary inner;
    inner.set("x", 10.0);
    inner.set("y", 20.0);
    d.set("pos", @inner);
    
    string json, err;
    json_stringify(d, json, err);
    
    // parse it back
    dictionary back;
    json_parse(json, back, err);

Copy

    void DumpDict(const string &in label, dictionary &in d)
    {
        log(label);
        
        array<string>@ keys = d.getKeys();
        for (uint i = 0; i < keys.length(); i++)
        {
            string k = keys[i];
            // Try double first
            double dv;
            string sv;
            bool gotDouble = d.get(k, dv);
            bool gotString = d.get(k, sv);
            
            string vStr;
            if (gotDouble)
            vStr = "double " + k + " = " + dv;
            else if (gotString)
            vStr = "string " + k + " = \"" + sv + "\"";
            else
            vStr = "key " + k + " (unsupported type in dump)";
            
            log("  " + vStr);
        }
    }
    
    void TestBasicParse()
    {
        log("[1] Basic json_parse / json_decode");
        
        const string jsonText = """
        {
            "number": 123,
            "float":  3.14,
            "bool_true": true,
            "bool_false": false,
            "text": "hello",
            "object": { "x": 10, "y": 20 }
        }
        """;
        
        dictionary d;
        string err;
        
        if (!json_parse(jsonText, d, err))
        {
            log_error("  [FAIL] json_parse failed: " + err);
            return;
        }
        log("  [ OK ] json_parse succeeded");
        DumpDict("  Dump of parsed dictionary:", d);
        
        // Basic checks
        double num = 0;
        double flt = 0;
        string txt;
        
        if (d.get("number", num) && num == 123)
        log("  [ OK ] number == 123");
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] number != 123");
        
        if (d.get("float", flt) && flt > 3.13 && flt < 3.15)
        log("  [ OK ] float ~= 3.14");
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] float ~= 3.14");
        
        if (d.get("text", txt) && txt == "hello")
        log("  [ OK ] text == \"hello\"");
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] text != \"hello\"");
        
        // bools are stored as doubles (1.0 / 0.0)
        double bt = 0, bf = 1;
        d.get("bool_true", bt);
        d.get("bool_false", bf);
        if (bt == 1.0 && bf == 0.0)
        log("  [ OK ] bool_true/false mapped to 1.0/0.0");
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] bool mapping incorrect");
        
        // Test alias json_decode
        dictionary d2;
        string err2;
        if (json_decode("{\"a\":1,\"b\":2}", d2, err2))
        log("  [ OK ] json_decode succeeded");
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] json_decode failed: " + err2);
    }
    
    void TestInvalidParse()
    {
        log("\n[2] Invalid JSON parse test");
        
        dictionary d;
        string err;
        
        const string badJson = "{ invalid json !!! }";
        bool ok = json_parse(badJson, d, err);
        if (!ok)
        {
            log("  [ OK ] json_parse returned false for invalid JSON");
            log("        error: " + err);
        }
        else
        {
            log_error("  [FAIL] json_parse unexpectedly succeeded on invalid JSON");
        }
    }
    
    void TestStringifyRoundtrip()
    {
        log("\n[3] json_stringify / json_encode roundtrip");
        
        dictionary d;
        d.set("hello", "world");
        d.set("num", 42.0);          // numbers are stored as double
        d.set("float", 1.5);
        d.set("flag_bool", true);    // bool (script side)
        d.set("flag_num", 1.0);      // numeric boolean
        
        // nested object
        dictionary nested;
        nested.set("x", 10.0);
        nested.set("y", 20.0);
        d.set("nested", @nested);
        
        DumpDict("  Original dictionary:", d);
        
        string json;
        string err;
        
        if (!json_stringify(d, json, err))
        {
            log_error("  [FAIL] json_stringify failed: " + err);
            return;
        }
        
        log("  [ OK ] json_stringify succeeded");
        log("  JSON: " + json);
        
        // Roundtrip: parse back
        dictionary back;
        string err2;
        if (!json_parse(json, back, err2))
        {
            log_error("  [FAIL] parse(stringify(...)) failed: " + err2);
            return;
        }
        
        log("  [ OK ] parse(stringify(...)) succeeded");
        DumpDict("  Decoded dictionary:", back);
        
        // Test alias json_encode
        string json2, err3;
        if (json_encode(d, json2, err3))
        log("  [ OK ] json_encode succeeded: " + json2);
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] json_encode failed: " + err3);
    }
    
    void TestNullAndArrays()
    {
        log("\n[4] Null and array handling note");
        
        const string txt = """
        {
            "a": 1,
            "b": null,
            "c": [1,2,3]
        }
        """;
        
        dictionary d;
        string err;
        
        if (!json_parse(txt, d, err))
        {
            log_error("  [FAIL] parse failed: " + err);
            return;
        }
        
        DumpDict("  Parsed dictionary:", d);
        
        // "b" is null -> omitted
        double a = 0;
        bool hasB = d.exists("b");
        d.get("a", a);
        
        if (a == 1.0 && !hasB)
        log("  [ OK ] null field skipped, 'a' present");
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] null or 'a' handling incorrect");
        
        // "c" is an array -> currently skipped
        if (!d.exists("c"))
        log("  [ OK ] array key 'c' skipped as expected");
        else
        log_error("  [FAIL] array key 'c' unexpectedly present");
    }
    
    int main()
    {
        log("=== JSON API Test Begin (AngelScript) ===");
        
        TestBasicParse();
        TestInvalidParse();
        TestStringifyRoundtrip();
        TestNullAndArrays();
        
        log("=== JSON API Test End ===");
        return 0;
    }

---

# Net API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The **Net API** provides AngelScript access to:

*   **HTTP(S)** requests
    
*   **WebSocket** (ws / wss) connections
    
*   Background message buffering
    
*   Safe multi-threaded operation
    
*   Automatic cleanup on script unload
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#overview)

Overview

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#http)

HTTP

*   `net_http_get(url, status, body, timeout_ms)`
    
*   `net_http_post(url, content_type, body, status, out_body, timeout_ms)`
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#websocket)

WebSocket

*   `ws_t ws_connect(url, timeout_ms)`
    
*   `ws_t` methods:
    
    *   `is_open()`
        
    *   `send_text()`
        
    *   `send_json()`
        
    *   `send_binary()`
        
    *   `recv()` (blocking)
        
    *   `poll()` (non-blocking)
        
    *   `close()`
        
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#supported-url-schemes)

Supported URL Schemes

Type

Schemes

HTTP

`http://`, `https://`

WebSocket

`ws://`, `wss://`

Hostnames

`example.com`, `sub.domain.net`

IPs

`127.0.0.1`, `192.168.x.x`

Ports

Fully supported: `ws://ip:port/path`

> `ws://` and `wss://` automatically map to WinHTTP’s `http://` / `https://` internally.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#http-api)

HTTP API


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-net_http_get)

`bool net_http_get(...)`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#parameters)

Parameters

Name

Type

Description

`url`

`string`

Full URL (`https://httpbin.org/get`)

`status_code`

`out uint`

HTTP status (200, 404, etc.)

`body`

`out string`

Response body

`timeout_ms`

`uint`

Optional timeout (resolve/connect/send/receive)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#returns)

Returns

`true` = request succeeded (transport level, not HTTP success) `false` = network/connection error

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#example)

Example

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-net_http_post)

`bool net_http_post(...)`

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#example-1)

Example

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#websocket-api)

WebSocket API


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

WebSockets are exposed as a handle type:

Internally, each websocket:

*   Opens a WinHTTP WebSocket handle
    
*   Launches a **background message receive thread**
    
*   Buffers complete messages into a protected queue
    
*   Cleans up automatically on script unload (using AS ref-tracking like `proc_t`)
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#ws_t-ws_connect)

`ws_t ws_connect(...)`


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#return-value)

Return value

*   A valid `ws_t` handle on success
    
*   `0` on failure
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#example-2)

Example

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#websocket-methods)

WebSocket Methods


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All websocket operations are methods on the `ws_t` type.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-ws_t-is_open-const)

`bool ws_t::is_open() const`

Returns `true` while:

*   The socket is open, AND
    
*   The background receive thread is still running.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-ws_t-send_text-const-string-and-in-msg)

`bool ws_t::send_text(const string &in msg)`

Sends a UTF-8 text frame.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-ws_t-send_json-const-string-and-in-json)

`bool ws_t::send_json(const string &in json)`

Sends a JSON UTF-8 message.

Example:

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-ws_t-send_binary-const-array-less-than-uint8-greater-than-and-in-data)

`bool ws_t::send_binary(const array<uint8> &in data)`

Sends a binary WebSocket frame.

> Some public echo servers may close on binary frames. Your API supports them natively.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#receiving-messages)

Receiving Messages


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Messages are delivered as **complete frames** into an internal queue.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-ws_t-recv-string-and-out-msg-bool-and-out-is_text)

`bool ws_t::recv(string &out msg, bool &out is_text)`

Blocking receive (waits for next message).

*   Returns `true` when a message is dequeued.
    
*   Blocks with a 1ms sleep inside the engine.
    
*   Returns `false` if the socket closed and queue is empty.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#example-3)

Example

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#bool-ws_t-poll-string-and-out-msg-bool-and-out-is_text-bool-and-out-is_closed)

`bool ws_t::poll(string &out msg, bool &out is_text, bool &out is_closed)`

Non-blocking check.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#outcomes)

Outcomes

1.  **Message available**
    
    *   Returns `true`
        
    *   Fills `msg`
        
    *   `is_text = true/false`
        
    *   `is_closed` reflects final socket state
        
    
2.  **No message yet**
    
    *   Returns `false`
        
    *   `msg = ""`
        
    *   `is_closed = false`
        
    
3.  **Socket closed and queue empty**
    
    *   Returns `false`
        
    *   `is_closed = true`
        
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#example-frame-update)

Example (frame update)

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#closing)

Closing


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#void-ws_t-close-uint16-code-1000)

`void ws_t::close(uint16 code = 1000)`

*   Signals the receive thread to stop
    
*   Sends a close frame
    
*   Waits for the thread to terminate
    
*   Frees all WinHTTP handles
    
*   Removes itself from the internal AS websocket ref-tracker
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#example-4)

Example

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#automatic-cleanup-important)

Automatic Cleanup (Important)


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This API integrates with your existing **AngelScript resource tracking model**:

*   All websockets created within a script are tracked
    
*   On script unload, the engine loops through these refs and frees them
    

This guarantees:

*   No leaked sockets
    
*   No zombie threads
    
*   Safe hot-reload
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#full-example)

Full Example


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#summary)

Summary


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#http-1)

HTTP

*   `net_http_get(url, out status, out body, timeout)`
    
*   `net_http_post(url, content_type, body, out status, out response, timeout)`
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/net-api#websocket-1)

WebSocket

*   `ws_t ws_connect(url, timeout)`
    
*   `ws_t` methods:
    
    *   `is_open()`
        
    *   `send_text()`
        
    *   `send_json()`
        
    *   `send_binary()`
        
    *   `recv(out msg, out is_text)`
        
    *   `poll(out msg, out is_text, out is_closed)`
        
    *   `close(code)`

Copy

    bool net_http_get(
        const string &in url,
        uint &out status_code,
        string &out body,
        uint timeout_ms = 0
    );

Copy

    uint status;
    string body;
    
    bool ok = net_http_get("https://httpbin.org/get", status, body, 5000);
    
    if (ok)
    {
        log("GET " + status);
        log("Body: " + body);
    }

Copy

    bool net_http_post(
        const string &in url,
        const string &in content_type,
        const string &in body,
        uint &out status_code,
        string &out response,
        uint timeout_ms = 0
    );

Copy

    uint status;
    string response;
    
    bool ok = net_http_post(
        "https://httpbin.org/post",
        "application/json",
        "{\"hello\":\"pcx\"}",
        status,
        response,
        5000
    );

Copy

    ws_t ws_connect(const string &in url, uint timeout_ms = 0);

Copy

    ws_t ws_connect(const string &in url, uint timeout_ms = 0);

Copy

    ws_t ws = ws_connect("wss://ws.postman-echo.com/raw", 5000);
    if (ws == 0)
    {
        log("Connection failed");
        return;
    }
    log("Connected");

Copy

    ws.send_text("hello from AS!");

Copy

    ws.send_json("{\"type\":\"ping\",\"from\":\"as\"}");

Copy

    array<uint8> bin = { 0, 1, 2, 3 };
    ws.send_binary(bin);

Copy

    string msg;
    bool isText;
    
    if (ws.recv(msg, isText))
        log("Received: " + msg);

Copy

    string msg;
    bool text, closed;
    
    bool has = ws.poll(msg, text, closed);
    
    if (has)
    {
        log("WS message: " + msg);
    }
    else if (closed)
    {
        log("WS closed");
    }

Copy

    ws.close();

Copy

    int main()
    {
        uint status;
        string body;
        
        // HTTP
        if (net_http_get("https://httpbin.org/get", status, body, 3000))
        log("GET OK: " + status);
        
        // WS
        ws_t ws = ws_connect("wss://ws.postman-echo.com/raw", 3000);
    
        ws.send_text("hello from AS");
        
        string msg; bool text;
        if (ws.recv(msg, text))
        log("Echo: " + msg);
        
        ws.close();
        return 0;
    }

---

# GUI API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

The Lua GUI API allows scripts to dynamically create UI inside the Perception.cx interface. UI created by a script is **owned** by that script and is automatically removed when the script unloads.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#supported-features)

✔ Supported Features

*   Create subtabs inside the main UI
    
*   Add panels inside subtabs
    
*   Add UI elements inside panels
    
*   Read/write element values
    
*   Hide/show elements at runtime (`set_active`)
    
*   Keybinds, color pickers, and buttons that belong to a parent checkbox
    
*   List controls with highlight, insert, remove, set active index
    
*   Script-level button callbacks
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#ui-hierarchy)

**UI Hierarchy**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Copy

    Tab (index 0–4)
     └─ Subtab
          └─ Panel (small or large)
               ├─ Checkbox
               │     ├─ Keybind (child)
               │     └─ Color Picker(s) (child, up to 2)
               │     └─ Button (child)
               ├─ Slider (double or int)
               ├─ Input Text Box
               ├─ Multi Select
               ├─ Single Select
               ├─ List
               └─ Other elements…

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#element-creation-rules)

**Element Creation Rules**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#important-ordering-constraint)

🔥 **Important Ordering Constraint**

Some elements must be created _immediately after a checkbox_, because the UI engine uses the checkbox as their parent:

Child Element

Rule

**keybind**

MUST be created right after its parent checkbox (1 or 2 allowed)

**color picker**

MUST be created right after its parent checkbox (1 or 2 allowed)

If you break this rule, the element will not get created.

*   **2 color pickers**, or
    
*   **2 keybinds**, or
    
*   **1 color picker + 1 keybind**
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#global-entry)

**Global Entry**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Parameters**

Name

Type

Description

string

boolean

Starting state

`draw_title`

boolean (optional)

boolean (optional)

Internal protection flag

`draw_just_label`

boolean (optional)

When enabled, the checkbox is non-interactive and functions purely as a label. This is useful when you only want to attach a color picker or keybind without toggle behavior.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#full-example)

**Full Example**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#script-unload-behavior)

**Script Unload Behavior**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When a script unloads:

*   All subtabs created by it are deleted
    
*   All panels and elements inside them are deleted
    
*   All button callbacks are unregistered
    
*   No UI leftovers remain
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#lookup-api)

**Lookup API**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#ui.find_element-parent_tab_index-subtab_name-panel_name-element_name-type_string)

`ui.find_element(parent_tab_index, subtab_name, panel_name, element_name, type_string)`

Looks up an existing UI element anywhere in the menu and returns the correct Lua userdata (the same type returned when you created it with `panel:add_*`).

If nothing is found → returns `nil`.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#parameters-6)

**Parameters**

Name

Type

Description

`parent_tab_index`

integer (0–4)

Which main tab the subtab is in

`subtab_name`

string

Name of the subtab

`panel_name`

string

Name of the panel

`element_name`

string

Exact display name of the element

`type_string`

string

Type of the element (see table below)

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#valid-type_string-values)

**Valid** `**type_string**` **Values**

Type String

Returns

`"checkbox"`

`ui_checkbox`

`"slider_double"`

`ui_slider_double`

`"slider_int"`

`ui_slider_int`

`"input"`

`ui_input`

`"multi_select"`

`ui_multi_select`

`"single_select"`

`ui_single_select`

`"keybind"`

`ui_keybind`

`"color_picker"`

`ui_color`

`"button"`

`ui_button`

`"list"`

`ui_list`

* * *

Condition

Returns

Correct UI userdata (checkbox, slider, list, etc.)

Not found

`nil`

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#usage-examples)

**Usage Examples**

**Toggle a checkbox**

**Adjust a slider by name**

**Highlight list entry by name**

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#config-api)

🧾 **Config API**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Perception.cx supports saving/loading the entire UI configuration, including all elements, values, and states.

These two APIs allow Lua scripts to trigger that behavior.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#ui.construct_config-string)

`ui.construct_config() → string`

Builds a **full configuration snapshot** of all UI elements.

Returns a config string you can save to disk or use however you like.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#example-5)

Example

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#ui.apply_config-config_string)

`ui.apply_config(config_string)`

Applies a config previously generated by `ui.construct_config()`.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#example-6)

Example

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#ui.is_active)

`ui.is_active()`


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Checks if the gui is currently visible or not

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#name-prefixing-for-elements-prefix)

🏷 Name Prefixing for Elements (`##prefix_`)

The GUI API supports **name prefixing** so that multiple UI elements can share the **same visible label** while still being uniquely identified by the configuration system.

This is important when you have repeated layouts (per-player, per-item, etc.) and want each control to save/load separately.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#how-it-works)

How It Works

When you pass the `name` parameter to `panel:add_*`:

*   The part **after** `##prefix_` is the **visible label** shown in the UI and the rest is unique id
    
*   The **configuration system** (`ui.construct_config` / `ui.apply_config`) uses the **full prefixed name**
    
*   `ui.find_element(...)` **does not take prefix** and matches based on the **visible label only**
    

So:

Both controls render as:

> Player Name

…but their internal IDs and config entries are different.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#duplicate-names-and-config-behavior)

Duplicate Names and Config Behavior

*   **Duplicate visible names are allowed even without prefixes.** The UI will render and behave normally.
    
*   However, **without prefixes**, the internal configuration system **cannot uniquely differentiate** those elements:
    
    *   Their saved values can overwrite each other
        
    *   Loading a config may apply the wrong value to the wrong element
        
    
*   With `##prefix_`, each element has a distinct internal ID, so:
    
    *   `ui.construct_config()` stores them separately
        
    *   `ui.apply_config()` restores each one correctly
        
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#ui.find_element-and-prefixes)

`ui.find_element` and Prefixes

*   `element_name` is matched against the **visible name only** (the part after `##`).
    
*   If multiple elements share the same visible label:
    
    *   `ui.find_element` will return the **first matching element** of that type in that panel.
        
    

Example:

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#when-to-use-prefixing)

When to Use Prefixing

Use the `##prefix_` pattern whenever:

*   You have **multiple elements with the same visible label** in the same panel/subtab.
    
*   You care that each element’s value is **saved and loaded distinctly** via the config system.
    

Example pattern:

All rows show **“Player Name”**, but each has its own internal ID and config entry.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/gui-api#reference-tracking-internal-behavior)

🔒 **Reference Tracking (Internal Behavior)**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Whenever you call:

The element is automatically tracked by the script. If the element is destroyed elsewhere (e.g., its panel or subtab is removed), the script can safely unregister that reference later.

(You do **not** need to manage this manually — it is just here for understanding the lifecycle.)

[PreviousProc APIchevron-left](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/proc-api)
[NextSystem API (CPU & Disassembly)chevron-right](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/lua-script/system-api-cpu-and-disassembly)

# Win API | Perception AngelScript & Lua API

This API allows AngelScript scripts to interact with Windows:

*   Find windows by title or class
    
*   Read window titles, classes, positions, sizes
    
*   Detect whether a window is foreground or active
    
*   Read or write clipboard text
    
*   Discover the thread & process IDs for a window
    
*   Send messages (WM\_CHAR, WM\_KEYDOWN, WM\_KEYUP, etc.)
    
*   Send global keyboard/mouse events (SendInput)
    

Handles (`hwnd`) are represented as **uint64** values.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#window-lookup)

**Window Lookup**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#uint64-find_window-const-string-and-in-title)

`uint64 find_window(const string &in title)`

Finds a top-level window by its title.

Returns 0 if not found.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#window-enumeration)

Window Enumeration

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#array-less-than-windowinfo-greater-than-get_all_hwnds)

`array<WindowInfo>@ get_all_hwnds()`

Enumerates all top-level windows on the system and returns detailed information about each.

**Returns:** Handle to an array of `WindowInfo` objects, or `null` on failure.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#windowinfo-type)

WindowInfo Type

A value type containing window details:

Property

Type

Description

`hwnd`

`uint64`

Window handle

`pid`

`uint`

Process ID

`tid`

`uint`

Thread ID

`process_name`

`string`

Executable name (e.g., `"notepad.exe"`)

`title`

`string`

Window title text

`class_name`

`string`

Window class name

**Example:**

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#uint64-find_window-const-string-and-in-title-const-string-and-in-classname)

`uint64 find_window(const string &in title, const string &in className)`

Finds a window by **title** and **class name**.

Pass empty string (`""`) to ignore a filter.

Returns 0 if not found.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#window-information)

**Window Information**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-get_window_size-uint64-hwnd-int-and-out-w-int-and-out-h)

`bool get_window_size(uint64 hwnd, int &out w, int &out h)`

Retrieves the window’s width and height (outer size).

Returns `false` if the window is invalid.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-get_window_rect-uint64-hwnd-int-and-out-x-int-and-out-y-int-and-out-w-int-and-out-h)

`bool get_window_rect(uint64 hwnd, int &out x, int &out y, int &out w, int &out h)`

Retrieves full window rect:

*   `x, y` — top-left screen coordinates
    
*   `w, h` — size in pixels
    

Returns `false` on failure.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-get_window_title-uint64-hwnd-string-and-out-title)

`bool get_window_title(uint64 hwnd, string &out title)`

Gets the window’s title text (UTF-8).

*   Returns `true` even for empty titles.
    
*   Returns `false` only when the hwnd is invalid.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-get_window_class-uint64-hwnd-string-and-out-cls)

`bool get_window_class(uint64 hwnd, string &out cls)`

Gets the Win32 window class name.

Returns `false` if the window is invalid.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#foreground-activity)

**Foreground / Activity**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-set_foreground_window-uint64-hwnd)

`bool set_foreground_window(uint64 hwnd)`

Attempts to bring the window to foreground.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-is_foreground_window-uint64-hwnd)

`bool is_foreground_window(uint64 hwnd)`

Returns `true` if the given window is currently foreground.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-is_window_active-uint64-hwnd)

`bool is_window_active(uint64 hwnd)`

Checks whether the window:

*   is valid
    
*   is visible
    
*   is **not minimized**
    

This is a broader “is active” check.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#clipboard)

**Clipboard**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All clipboard strings are UTF-8.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-copy_to_clipboard-const-string-and-in-text)

`bool copy_to_clipboard(const string &in text)`

Copies text into the Windows clipboard.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-copy_from_clipboard-string-and-out-text)

`bool copy_from_clipboard(string &out text)`

Reads text from the Windows clipboard.

*   Returns `true` if any text was successfully retrieved.
    
*   Empty clipboard → empty string.
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#thread-and-process-info)

**Thread & Process Info**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-get_window_thread_process_id-uint64-hwnd-uint-and-out-tid-uint-and-out-pid)

`bool get_window_thread_process_id(uint64 hwnd, uint &out tid, uint &out pid)`

Retrieves:

*   `tid` — thread ID
    
*   `pid` — process ID
    

Returns `false` if the hwnd is invalid.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#messaging)

**Messaging**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-post_message-uint64-hwnd-uint-msg-uint64-wparam-uint64-lparam)

`bool post_message(uint64 hwnd, uint msg, uint64 wparam, uint64 lparam)`

Posts a raw Win32 message to a window.

Examples:

*   `post_message(hwnd, 0x0010, 0, 0)` → WM\_CLOSE
    
*   `post_message(hwnd, 0x0100, VK_A, 0)` → WM\_KEYDOWN for ‘A’
    

Returns `false` if the hwnd is invalid.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#keyboard-input)

**Keyboard Input**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#global-keyboard-sendinput)

Global keyboard (SendInput)

These functions simulate real keyboard events globally.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-win_key_down-uint-vk)

`void win_key_down(uint vk)`

Simulates a key-down.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-win_key_up-uint-vk)

`void win_key_up(uint vk)`

Simulates a key-up.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-win_key_press-uint-vk-uint-delay_ms-30)

`void win_key_press(uint vk, uint delay_ms = 30)`

Press → delay → release.

*   `delay_ms` clamped to `0..1000`.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#window-targeted-typing-postmessage)

Window-targeted typing (PostMessage)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-send_char-uint64-hwnd-const-string-and-in-text)

`bool send_char(uint64 hwnd, const string &in text)`

Sends a single character to a window using `WM_CHAR`.

*   Only the **first UTF-16 code unit** is used.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#bool-send_key-uint64-hwnd-uint-vk)

`bool send_key(uint64 hwnd, uint vk)`

Sends:

*   `WM_KEYDOWN`
    
*   `WM_KEYUP`
    

…to a specific window.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#mouse-input)

**Mouse Input**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Mouse input uses real global `SendInput` events.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-mouse_move-int-x-int-y)

`void mouse_move(int x, int y)`

Moves the mouse to absolute screen coordinates.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-mouse_move_relative-int-dx-int-dy)

`void mouse_move_relative(int dx, int dy)`

Moves the mouse relative to the current cursor position.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-mouse_left_click)

`void mouse_left_click()`

Left button click.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-mouse_right_click)

`void mouse_right_click()`

Right button click.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-mouse_middle_click)

`void mouse_middle_click()`

Middle button click.

Each sends DOWN → small wait → UP.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-mouse_scroll-int-amount)

`void mouse_scroll(int amount)`

Scroll amount in “wheel notches”:

*   positive → scroll up
    
*   negative → scroll down
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#void-send_mouse_input-int64-dx-int64-dy-uint-flags-uint-mouse_data)

`void send_mouse_input(int64 dx, int64 dy, uint flags, uint mouse_data)`

Send input manually via raw input.

* * *

[hashtag](https://docs.perception.cx/perception-angel-script-api/angel-script/win-api#util)

**Util**


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`int64 get_tickcount64()`

*   GetTickCount64()

Copy

    int main()
    {
        array<WindowInfo>@ windows = get_all_hwnds();
        
        if (windows is null)
        {
            log("Failed to get windows list");
            return 0;
        }
        
        log("Found " + windows.length() + " windows\n");
        
        for (uint i = 0; i < windows.length(); i++)
        {
            WindowInfo w = windows[i];
            
            if (w.title.isEmpty())
               continue;
            
            log("=== Window " + (i + 1) + " ===");
            log("  HWND:         " + w.hwnd);
            log("  PID:          " + w.pid);
            log("  TID:          " + w.tid);
            log("  Process:      " + w.process_name);
            log("  Title:        " + w.title);
            log("  Class:        " + w.class_name);
            log("");
        }
        
        for (uint i = 0; i < windows.length(); i++)
        {
            if (windows[i].process_name == "notepad.exe")
            {
                log("Found Notepad! HWND: " + windows[i].hwnd);
                break;
            }
        }
          return 0;
    }
    
    

Copy

    string title;
    string cls;
    
    uint64 hwnd = find_window("Untitled - Notepad");
    
    if (hwnd != 0)
    {
        int x, y, w, h;
        get_window_rect(hwnd, x, y, w, h);
    
        get_window_title(hwnd, title);
        get_window_class(hwnd, cls);
    
        log("Title: " + title);
        log("Class: " + cls);
        log("Rect: " + x + "," + y + "  size " + w + "x" + h);
    }

    mouse_move(100, 200);
